Current Affairs Commentary

The Change of Chinese and Japanese Envoys

— Zi

Since our country's administrative center renewed the Ambassador to Japan, Chiang, returning to take on the important task of internal affairs, the heavy responsibility of sending an envoy to Japan has fallen on Xu Shiying, who has long been engaged in charity and relief work. Coincidentally, the Japanese Ambassador to China, Arita, was also recalled because the results of his activities in China were not satisfactory to his military, and Arita Hachiro, who had once advocated a "tough-on-China theory," was transferred from Belgium to take his place. Based on factual observations, this change of envoys in the two countries is due to ordinary administrative relations in our country, while in Japan it is a reason to change diplomatic actions. Since the internal situations are not the same, the points that deserve attention are inevitably of different importance.

Ambassador Akira Ariyoshi came to our country in September of the 21st year and has been in office for more than three years. When he first arrived, he adopted a policy of observing the situation quietly and taking advantage of opportunities to advance. In October of that year, it was reported that Ariyoshi had suggested to Foreign Minister Hirota to change his policy toward China and oppose the invasion of Jehol, and at the same time, it was reported that Japan would change its envoy to China and replace him with Arita. If the people of the country can still remember the old news from three years ago, then observing the current situation will allow them to have a considerable understanding of Japan's future after the change of envoys. The reporter states this not to use the issue of the people of the Japanese mission as the basis for the discussion of Sino-Japanese relations. In the past five years, Japan's actions against us have been entirely directed by its Sanzhai Saka military headquarters and the Kwantung Army authorities in Changchun. The Kaskigase chief brain cannot have independent opinions, let alone the envoys who are ordered to do things. When it is suitable for quiet observation, employ quiet observers; when it is suitable for advance, employ tough figures. The appraisal is fixed to change with the environment, but as for its relationship with our country and the consequences, it depends only on how our diplomatic authorities deal with it.

Since the rumor of the Sino-Japanese Nanjing Conference has spread for more than a month, if it can really be realized, then China's pursuit of international coexistence with the most patient attitude is no less than the last test. Under such a situation, China is still trying to mediate the relations between the two countries, not willing to be infinitely humiliated. If the situation in the future reaches a degree that China cannot tolerate or force, China cannot but seek another way to survive. The reporter believes that if the Nanjing Conference does not become a bubble, Ambassador Arita's coming to China will be responsible for the negotiation. Will it create a situation that China must find another way to survive, or will it change the will of the aggressors in its country with independent diplomatic opinions? The Chinese are paying attention to this new envoy in the neighboring country.

Finally, the reporter also expresses considerable expectations for Xu Shiying, who has shouldered the heavy responsibility of sending an envoy to Japan. Xu has been in charge of the judiciary for more than ten years in the late Qing Dynasty and the early Republic of China. After the second year of the Republic, he entered politics and was still able to cope with ease. He has also presided over relief work for many years and has a reputation in society. Now he has assumed the diplomatic responsibility with generosity. Although he is not a master of diplomacy, he must be confident in fulfilling his mission. Under the current situation of the two countries, even if the foreign mission does not have the power to preside over the country's fortune, it often makes the already lost sovereignty slightly recovered, and the future situation does not become worse. Can Xu meet the expectations of the people of the country?

The Rise and Fall of Italian and German Power: France Consolidates its Position in Central Europe

Negotiating Military Matters with Romania

Seeking Understanding with Yugoslavia as well

London – As Germany grows stronger and Italy is temporarily unable to operate on the European stage, France, recognizing this situation, is eager to consolidate its alliances in Central and Eastern Europe. Therefore, the talks with monarchs and high officials of various countries who passed through Paris on their way back home after attending the funeral rites of King George are noteworthy. These meetings seem to have two purposes: 1. To dispel any possible misunderstandings arising from the current situation. 2. To solidify the commitment of those who safeguard peace to adhere to the collective security system. According to French political commentators, some countries, including Romania and Yugoslavia, have recently shown a tendency towards Germany. Paris is concerned about this and is now taking the opportunity to dispel these concerns. Romania has already reached an understanding with France, and today's talks between French Foreign Minister Flandin and Prince Paul of Yugoslavia are expected to produce similar assurances. (Reuters, 4th)

Paris – Six diplomats, politicians, and administrative leaders, led by French Foreign Minister Flandin and King Carol of Romania, held important talks today to restore the Danubian Pact negotiations and to consolidate the continental system of security. It is also noted that Soviet Foreign Minister Litvinov is visiting here to urge the French Chamber of Deputies to ratify the Franco-Soviet mutual assistance pact within this week. What is noteworthy is that the stipulations of this united front are disliked by Germany. Today, it was learned that these diplomatic negotiations may lead to a mutual assistance pact between the Soviet Union and Romania. (National Telegram, 3rd)

Paris – Diplomatic talks here are constantly changing, making them almost impossible to grasp. Therefore, in addition to what is published in the newspapers, there are also behind-the-scenes discussions. King Carol of Romania and the country’s Air Force Minister have consulted with the French Chief of Staff for a long time. It is reported that the King of Bulgaria expressed to the French Foreign Minister that his country will be loyal to the League of Nations. French newspapers consider the talks between Flandin and the Turkish Foreign Minister to be quite important because such talks not only concern the Italian-Abyssinian dispute and the Central European collective security system, but also involve the future distribution of the Balkan countries. (National Telegram, 4th)

It was recently heard in the Romanian capital that the Prime Minister and Minister of the Army, Tatarescu, will depart for Paris to negotiate military equipment issues after King Carol returns home. (Havas, 3rd)

French and Turkish Foreign Ministers Discuss Balkan Issues

Bulgaria is Willing to Support the League of Nations

Paris – It is reported that Flandin met with Turkish Foreign Minister Rüştü this morning to discuss: 1. Mutual assistance in the Mediterranean. 2. Bulgaria's accession to the Balkan Entente. As for whether the redeployment of fortifications in Turkey's Dardanelles and Bosphorus straits was discussed, it is still unknown. Regarding this matter, it is generally believed that Turkey thinks it is inappropriate to raise the issue of the straits at this time because Germany may soon demand to redeploy fortifications on the left bank of the Rhine. (Havas, 3rd)

Paris – King Carol of Romania recently gave an interview to a reporter from "Le Petit Parisien," saying that the issue of concluding the Danubian Pact has made great progress since the authorities of various countries held talks in London and Paris recently. As for maintaining Austria's independence, although previous efforts have failed, he remains optimistic. The newspaper also reported that King Boris of Bulgaria told French Foreign Minister Flandin during their meeting yesterday that Bulgaria is determined to make the League of Nations Covenant its ultimate destination and is prepared to cooperate effectively with the League of Nations. (Havas News Agency, 4th)

Paris – King Boris of Bulgaria recently visited President Lebrun at the Presidential Palace and inspected a detachment of the public guard. The talks lasted for an hour. After leaving the palace, he received Premier Sarraut, Foreign Minister Flandin, and personnel from the Bulgarian embassy at his residence. Turkish Foreign Minister Rüştü visited Foreign Minister Flandin this morning, and then went to the Premier's Office at 4 PM to pay respects to Premier Sarraut. He is scheduled to visit Minister of Commerce Pomaret at 10 AM tomorrow to discuss the adjustment of the Franco-Turkish commercial agreement, and then visit President Lebrun at the Presidential Palace. Hungarian Foreign Minister Kánya left for home this afternoon. After arriving here last Saturday, he only stayed for two days as a private citizen and did not hold any diplomatic talks with French politicians. Prince Paul, Regent of Yugoslavia, arrived here from London at 6 PM this afternoon, got off at the Gare du Nord, and went to the residence of Prince Nicholas of Greece. (Note: Prince Nicholas is Prince Paul's father-in-law and the father-in-law of the Duke of Kent, the fourth brother of the British King.) He is scheduled to visit Foreign Minister Flandin at 6 PM tomorrow afternoon. Austrian Vice-Chancellor Prince Starhemberg is also scheduled to visit Foreign Minister Flandin at 3 PM tomorrow afternoon. Lithuanian Foreign Minister Lozoraitis arrived here from London yesterday and visited Foreign Minister Flandin at 3:30 PM this afternoon. He is scheduled to leave for home tomorrow. King Carol of Romania received French Army Chief of Staff General Gamelin at the "Ritz" Hotel today. (Havas News Agency, 3rd)

Paris – President Lebrun is scheduled to visit King Boris of Bulgaria at the Bulgarian Embassy at 5 PM this afternoon. Prince Paul, Regent of Yugoslavia, is scheduled to visit President Lebrun at 4 PM this afternoon. In addition, French Premier Sarraut and Foreign Minister Flandin are scheduled to visit Prince Paul, Regent of Yugoslavia, at 5 PM and 6 PM, respectively. (Havas, 4th)

End of Paris Talks: French Foreign Minister Informs Britain

Content Focuses on Collective Movement

Paris – Foreign Minister Flandin recently met with British Ambassador to France, Sir Clerk, to inform Clerk of the results of his talks with King Carol of Romania, Foreign Minister Titulescu of Romania, King Boris of Bulgaria, and Turkish Foreign Minister Rüştü. According to sources from this agency, the talks held in Paris at this time focused on the organization of the collective security system. In the Little Entente and the Balkan Entente countries, there is a strong desire to find a final and concrete interpretation of Article 16 of the League of Nations Covenant (i.e., the article concerning sanctions and mutual assistance measures) and the principles of collective security. (Havas, 3rd)

London – When Foreign Secretary Eden recently held talks with French Foreign Minister Flandin, it is reported that the issue of concluding a Mediterranean pact was considered. This matter has recently been confirmed by semi-official sources. It is said that the two were unable to proceed with negotiations due to the current situation of the Italian-Abyssinian issue, and they wanted to find a way to hold negotiations on the general issue of the Mediterranean system. This plan is not opposed in Britain, but it is believed that whether the outcome will be successful is still unknown. Therefore, the task of contacting Italy is entrusted to France. (Havas, 3rd)

Soviet Russia and Britain Review Changes in the European Situation

Deputy Minister of Defense Visits British Naval Chief of Staff

London – After Soviet Foreign Minister Litvinov departed for France, Deputy Minister of Defense General Tukhachevsky remained in Britain and visited British Naval Chief of Staff Sir Chatfield today. (Havas, 3rd)

London – When Soviet Foreign Minister Litvinov was in London the other day, he met with King Edward VIII and held talks with Foreign Secretary Eden. There has been much speculation about the relationship of these talks, some of which are excessive. Well-informed sources have clarified that the talks between the King, Foreign Secretary and Litvinov were purely of a general nature. The topics discussed were all previous issues and not related to the future situation. Both sides are pleased that the development of the European situation shows a trend towards collective action and reviewed the existing crises in Europe, among which the changes in German policy are particularly important. For example, the country's current intention to redeploy fortifications on the left bank of the Rhine is one example. Regarding this, Litvinov expressed deep concern, while Eden believes there is no imminent danger. This is the point of disagreement between the two. (Havas, 3rd)

Britain Strengthens National Defense: Germany Expresses Concern

But Also Spares No Effort in Rearming

Berlin – German newspapers expressed concern yesterday about Britain's talk of increasing national defense, but Germany is currently rearming at a rapid pace. It is learned that by the end of this year, Germany may complete the organization of the 36 divisions of the German army announced by German leader Hitler on May 1, 1935. At that time, Germany will have a standing army of more than 500,000 men, and the number of people who have undergone some training and can enter trench warfare will be at least 1.6 million. It is widely believed that the German Air Force currently has only 1,000 aircraft on the first line of defense, but this number will soon increase to 2,000. German aircraft factories are currently expanding actively, with the goal of manufacturing 4,000 aircraft per year. (Reuters, 4th)

Berlin – The Deutsche Allgemeine Zeitung recently published an article commenting on the diplomatic talks held by the authorities of various countries in London and Paris, especially the rapprochement between Britain and Russia, saying, "The political and diplomatic authorities of various countries first met in London and then gathered in Paris. This gathering is no less than a diplomatic conference. Among European politicians, the busiest is British Foreign Secretary Eden, and it is because of Eden that Soviet Foreign Minister Litvinov wants to interfere in Western European affairs. The new strategies being planned in London and Paris are nothing more than making the Soviet Union's position in Western Europe the same as the position Italy wants to assume in the Balkan Peninsula." (Havas, 3rd)

Berlin – The Frankfurter Zeitung recently published an editorial discussing various current events, especially two issues: the demilitarized zone on the Rhine and the collective security plan. It said, "The Treaty of Versailles unilaterally abolished Germany's armaments on the Rhine. If this provision is to be respected, the countries concerned must not undermine the Locarno Pact with unilateral military agreements or other means that are unfavorable to Germany. The Locarno Pact also reaffirmed the demilitarized zone on the Rhine. In addition, the Treaty of Versailles also has other unilateral provisions that Germany does not recognize, such as the internationalization of German waterways, the tragic phenomenon of the Memel autonomous region, and the establishment of mandated territories. The latter is the most important, and the purpose of the countries that initiated this system was to deprive Germany of its colonies." The newspaper then expressed its disagreement with the various local pacts concluded by various countries, saying that they have exceeded the scope of arbitration or neutrality. "The problem is that after the conclusion of active mutual assistance measures, there may not necessarily be a sense of security between each other. In short, if the collective security system is to live up to its name, the countries concerned must not, at least, establish treaties of a military nature or agreements similar to alliances. Only in this way can other countries be attracted to join happily." (Havas, 4th)

Czech Prime Minister Will Respond to Visit from Austrian Authorities

First to Paris and Yugoslavia

Czech Capital – The University of Paris will soon hold a celebration for former Czech President Masaryk. League of Nations Expert Committee Studies Oil Embargo Against Italy

Rapidly Drafting Report

Italy Considers Boycott Measures

Numbers Published on Global Petroleum Trade

Geneva – The League of Nations Expert Committee held its first meeting here today. Mexican Ambassador to Paris Gómez served as chairman. Gómez is the most vocal advocate for an oil embargo. The following countries participated in the meeting: Britain, France, Iraq, Iran, Mexico, Norway, Netherlands, Peru, Romania, Sweden, Soviet Russia, and Venezuela. Argentina was also invited to participate but did not send a representative. Uruguay and Cuba both stated they would send representatives but did not appear. Venezuela only attended as an observer. (National Telegram, 3rd)

Geneva – The Expert Committee held two resolutions in a meeting today to study the oil embargo against Italy. It will hold a second meeting tomorrow. The committee hopes to complete its report by the end of this week for the consideration of the Committee of Eighteen. Qualified observers here believe that a majority of the Committee of Eighteen will support implementing the oil embargo on a scheduled date because the implementation of the oil embargo has already been agreed upon in principle. (Reuters, 3rd)

Geneva – The League of Nations Expert Committee is drafting measures to implement an embargo on petroleum against Italy. Today, it considered rumors that Poland refused to participate in the oil embargo to be unfounded and said that the League of Nations has not invited Poland to send a representative because only countries that produce and export petroleum are invited to attend. (National Telegram, 3rd)

Geneva – The Expert Committee on the petroleum embargo issue recently appointed representatives from Britain, the Netherlands, and Norway to form a committee to study the transportation of petroleum and its by-products imported by Italy. It was decided to study the following points: 1. The carrying capacity of Italian oil tankers. 2. The carrying capacity of oil tankers flying the flags of non-League of Nations member states, whether they can be used to load oil for Italy currently or in the future. 3. Whether non-League of Nations member states can only use their own ships for their own commercial purposes (referring to not transporting petroleum for other countries). 4. Where all petroleum is loaded and where it is transported to. 5. Indirect transportation (i.e., oil produced by League of Nations member states is first transported to ports of non-member states and then re-exported to Italy). (Havas, 3rd)

Geneva – Representatives from twelve League of Nations member states that are also oil-producing countries have gradually taken action to embargo oil against Italy. At the same time, after economic experts made preliminary studies on various issues related to the oil embargo against Italy, two subcommittees have been established. One is studying whether Italy's petroleum supply can be completely cut off, and the other is studying whether Italy can be fatally struck after all oil transportation activities are completely prohibited. (National Telegram, 3rd)

Geneva – The Expert Committee on the petroleum embargo issue appointed by the Committee of Eighteen of the League of Nations met today and published the following figures after reviewing the global petroleum trade situation:

The total global petroleum production in 1934-1935 was 206,000,000 tons, of which the United States produced 88,000,000 tons, the Soviet Union produced 15,000,000 tons, Venezuela produced 14,000,000 tons, Romania produced 5,500,000 tons, Iran produced 4,500,000 tons, Mexico produced 1,400,000 tons, Iraq produced 340,000 tons, Colombia produced 160,000 tons, and Argentina produced 140,000 tons. The total amount of petroleum transported by ships from various countries in the same year was 8,400,000 tons, of which British and American ships each transported 2,400,000 tons, Norwegian ships transported 1,500,000 tons, and French ships transported 400,000 tons. (Havas, 3rd)

Rome – The Ministry of Vocational Groups recently appointed several experts to form a committee whose task is to draft a production plan for petroleum substitutes and study Italy's capabilities for this production business. In addition, the Official Gazette recently published an order that all merchants who manufacture and sell alcoholic beverages must report the current and annual production quantities to the authorities because the government may plan to replace petroleum with alcohol in the future to counter the petroleum embargo measures. (Havas, 3rd)

Rome – The Italian semi-official newspaper "The Voice of Fascism" revealed today that if the League of Nations takes an oil embargo against Italy, Italy will only have to use poison gas extensively in Abyssinian territory to retaliate. In short, Italy is determined to resist sanctions to the best of its ability. At the same time, the Official Gazette reported on the situation on the southern front, claiming that the Italian army led by General Graziani is currently engaged in hand-to-hand combat with the remnants of Abyssinian General Ras Desta. (National Telegram, 3rd)

Abyssinian Army Heavily Encircles, Capture of Makale Imminent

Water Sources Cut Off, Isolating Italian Army

Abyssinian Army Actively Reinforcing Southern Front

Abyssinian Capital – According to unconfirmed reports from the northern front, the Abyssinian army will recapture Makale imminently because the Abyssinian army has surrounded the city and cut off the main water source that Makale relies on. Furthermore, the Italian troops defending Makale are now isolated due to the long transportation routes.

Abyssinian Capital – According to war reports received today, the battles on both fronts are very calm. In the southern and southwestern provinces, the Abyssinian army is implementing a large-scale reorganization. Twenty thousand troops are acting on the front line, and the weak points of the front line have been strengthened with troops. A rapid reinforcement team of 50,000 men has now begun to be organized, which can provide assistance at any time in case of unexpected attacks. After three weeks of heavy rain, the weather has cleared up today, which is very convenient for the Abyssinian army's actions. This rapid military action is also due to the anticipation of the rainy season. Once the rainy season begins, it will be very difficult for the large army to act. At the same time, the work of training new troops in the capital and other places is being intensified. (Havas, 3rd)

Paris – Prime Minister Mussolini met with a reporter from "Le Paris Soir" in Rome, saying that he has great confidence in the new developments in the war in Abyssinia and firmly believes that the final victory will not belong to Abyssinia. The imminent rainy season will not reduce his optimism. He said that if it rains for four hours a day and the rest of the time is expected to be sunny, this alone is enough to maintain the morale of the Italian army. On the contrary, the Abyssinian army may have difficulty transporting weapons and food. Mussolini said that in any case, the rainy season cannot stop the Italian army from advancing. Although the difficulties in the front are great, the Italian army can eventually advance slowly. (National News Agency, 3rd)

Naval Issues: Britain and the United States Have a Secret Agreement

Established Around October Last Year

London – According to what our naval correspondent knows, France and Italy have expressed hesitation about inviting Germany to participate. However, this matter is secondary. The most important issue at present is the tonnage of battleships. Britain and the United States advocate 35,000 tons, while France and Italy demand a reduction to 27,000 tons. Each holds its own view and insists on it, and the situation is enough to hinder the future of the Four-Power Agreement. From the perspective of France and Italy, Britain originally advocated 25,000 tons as the tonnage of battleships and considered the 27,000 tons proposed by France to be too high. Now it has suddenly changed its attitude, which is difficult to understand. Some political figures believe that Britain and the United States established a secret agreement in October last year, and the content of which is still unknown to the outside world. The reason why Britain is accommodating the United States' position on the issue of battleship tonnage is precisely because of this. (Havas News Agency, 3rd)

Germany Has Not Complied with the London Naval Agreement

Britain Indicates that it Will Not Invite Germany to Participate in the Meeting for the Time Being

London – The London Naval Conference may encounter new difficulties. It is heard that lawyers have discovered that Germany has not complied with the Anglo-German Naval Treaty on limiting the tonnage of warships. The Naval Conference is currently dealing with qualitative restrictions. Britain is advocating inviting Germany to participate in the conference at an appropriate time, but it is heard that France is vigorously opposing Germany's participation in the discussion. At the same time, the dispute between the French and American representatives over the model of battleships has also dimmed the atmosphere for establishing an understanding on qualitative restrictions. It is heard that the United States has accepted Britain's request and will no longer build large cruisers, on the condition that the tonnage of each battleship is limited to 35,000 tons. However, France insists on a limit of 27,000 tons. The above two points are currently being dealt with in informal talks. At the same time, the subcommittee has approved the principle proposed by the United States to extend the age of battleships to 26 years. (Reuters, 4th)

London – Regarding the issue of inviting Germany to participate in the Naval Conference, British officials recently stated that Britain does not intend to invite Germany to participate hastily before the Four-Power Naval Agreement is negotiated. However, it is believed that the naval agreement can hardly be effective unless it is of a universal nature or has a considerable degree of universality. Britain is currently considering inviting Germany and other countries to participate once the Four-Power Agreement is negotiated. As for whether this issue has been raised for discussion at the conference, France has not yet expressed any objection. (Havas, 4th)

London – The expert subcommittee organized by the General Committee of the Naval Conference continued to discuss the definitions of various warships this afternoon. According to what our correspondent knows, the subcommittee has not yet established any concrete agreement, but has decided to continue working according to the following principles: 1. The distinction between battleships and cruisers is often based on the armaments installed on the ships, as stipulated in the Washington Treaty. If the German pocket battleship "Deutschland" has a gun caliber of 10 inches, which is not the 8 inches stipulated by the Washington Treaty for Class A cruisers, it should still be classified as a battleship. 2. The definition of aircraft carriers should still be based on what is stated in the Washington Treaty, that is, any warship, regardless of the number of aircraft it carries, should not be considered an aircraft carrier if it does not have the characteristics of an aircraft carrier (referring to the deck for aircraft takeoff and landing). In addition, the subcommittee accepted the US request today to increase the service age of battleships from 20 years to 26 years. This measure extends the service life of 35,000-ton battleships without having to rush to replace them, thereby increasing expenses. As for whether small warships such as shallow-water coastal defense ships should also be subject to qualitative restrictions, it is currently pending resolution. (Havas, 3rd)

US Neutrality Act: Fierce Debate in Congress

Senate Still Divided

Washington - The fierce debate in Congress regarding the US Neutrality Act may result in expanding current neutrality restrictions and prohibiting loans to belligerent nations. The Senate Foreign Relations Committee remains divided, and newspapers nationwide also have differing opinions, reflecting the public's concerned state regarding the neutrality issue. (Reuters dispatch on the 3rd)

Washington - Former International Court of Justice Judge Moore today launched a major attack on the government's Neutrality Act, calling it a ridiculous measure that not only fails to aid peace but could even promote war. Moore told the Foreign Relations Committee that the danger of the bill lies in granting the government the authority, in the name of promoting peace, to act in a non-neutral manner. He stated that Section Four of the bill grants the president the power to control exports, which will inevitably lead to favoring one side and being drawn into the conflict. This will also invite armed resistance from those capable of retaliation. Furthermore, using peacetime raw material export volumes as a standard is also unhelpful because if the US wants to export these materials to both warring parties, it must bear the responsibility of protecting the transport ships. Mr. [蒲氏] believes the main purpose of this bill is simply to cooperate with the League of Nations. Meanwhile, Chinese Ambassador to the US, Shih Chao-chi, gave a speech at the 列丘曼 Women's Club, expressing opinions that differed greatly from those mentioned above. Mr. Shih urged the audience to strengthen international cooperation to prevent aggressive nations unbound by the non-war pact and the League of Nations charter, and urged the US not to be satisfied with a form of isolationist neutrality. (National Telegraph on the 3rd)

Anglo-Egyptian Treaty Negotiations to Be Held in Cairo Mid-Month

London - Rumors circulating that Britain and Egypt will hold negotiations here to conclude a treaty are now denied by well-informed sources. They say that these negotiations will take place in Cairo, the capital of Egypt, and are unlikely to begin before mid-month. (Havas dispatch on the 3rd)

Current Greek Prime Minister to Form Coalition Cabinet

Former Agriculture Minister and Former Aviation Minister Do Not Cooperate

Athens - After the results of the parliamentary elections were announced, Prime Minister Demertzis submitted his resignation to King George II. The King, considering that the new parliament would not be convened until the 12th of this month, and that the divisions among the parties were not yet clear, retained Demertzis in office. According to reliable sources, Demertzis has been able to enlist the leaders of various political parties to form a coalition cabinet and will serve as Prime Minister himself. However, former Agriculture Minister Diaodos (who co-founded the United Party with the late Regent General Kondylis) and former Aviation Minister Rallis have already declared their refusal to cooperate with the Liberal Party led by former Prime Minister Venizelos because of their dissatisfaction with the reinstatement of military ranks to officers who participated in the revolution last March. Regarding the issue of the General Staff's opposition to the reinstatement of military ranks for officers, it is now known that the King has decided to appoint Prime Minister Demertzis to be responsible for conducting negotiations with the leaders of various political parties. If this can be resolved satisfactorily, all political problems can be solved easily. (Havas dispatch on the 4th)

Three Ministries of Japan - Foreign Affairs, Army, and Navy - Agree on Policies Towards China and Russia

The Three Principles of Hirota Remain Central to Policy Toward China

Determining the Russian-Manchurian Border - Negotiations to Be Submitted to Russia

Tokyo - Japan, in order to consolidate its China policy, is implementing a unified front. It has decided to recall Ambassador to China, Ariyoshi, and replace him with Ambassador to Belgium, Arita. It has also decided to expand and strengthen its garrison in China in mid-May, based on its activities in North China. Recently, the military attaché at the Japanese Embassy in China, Major General Isoya, was ordered to return home to provide a detailed explanation of our country's political situation. It is reported that after Ambassador Ariyoshi returns home, the Japanese government will hold a joint meeting of the three ministries—Foreign Affairs, Army, and Navy—centered on the new Ambassador to China, Arita, to determine a detailed policy towards China. This policy towards China will continue to center on the Three Principles of Hirota, with the aim of realizing them. Ambassador to China Arita and Major General Isoya will return to China to negotiate after the Japanese government has decided on the second phase of its China policy. (Hualian Telegraph on the 4th)

Tokyo - Due to the tense situation on the Russian-Manchurian border, the Japanese Ministries of Foreign Affairs, Army, and Navy held a meeting at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs conference room at 1:00 PM on the 4th to discuss countermeasures. Attendees included Director-General of the European and Asian Affairs Bureau of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Togo; Director-General of the East Asian Affairs Bureau, Kuwashima; Director of the Army Ministry, Okamura; Squad Leader of the Soviet Russian Section, Kawahou; Squad Leader of the Manchurian-Mongolian Section, Kage; Chief of the Military Affairs Division, Murakami; and relevant officials from the Navy Ministry.

First, Directors-General Togo and Kuwashima explained the recent pro-French and British policies of the Soviet Union, the Soviet Union's propaganda regarding the secret Japanese-German treaty, and reported on the state of Soviet security work being carried out on the western border, and the joint anti-communism defense work being carried out on the eastern border. Then, the entire group discussed the mutiny of the Manchurian troops on the 29th and the Russian-Manchurian troop conflict on the 30th. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs put forward this decision for countermeasures at the meeting. According to the investigation by the local authorities, it is quite clear that the mutiny of the Manchurian troops was instigated by the Soviet Union. Furthermore, the conflict on the 30th occurred because Russian troops crossed the border. The Japanese government should lodge a serious protest to the Soviet Union. The root cause of such incidents occurring between Russia and Manchuria is the ambiguity of the national border, so the Soviet Union should be urged to express its attitude on the Manchurian-Russian border demarcation committee case that the Japanese government has proposed. After the Three Ministries meeting decided on countermeasures on the 4th, Foreign Minister Hirota instructed the ambassador to Russia to lodge a protest and, at the same time, begin negotiations with the Soviet ambassador to Japan to determine the border issue. (Dohmei News Agency dispatch on the 4th)

Moscow - The Soviet government authorities, on the 3rd, clarified the policy on handling border disputes in the name of the Far Eastern Command and proposed the formation of a fair investigation committee. The Soviet Union's so-called fair committee seems to be an investigation committee composed of third-party countries that do not include permanent affairs countries. The Soviet Union once advocated on October 12, 1935, to organize a mixed commission of the Russian, Japanese, and "Manchurian" three countries, and now it has decided to deal with border issues by the third-party committee, which is understandable that it attaches importance to the general nature of border issues. (Dohmei News Agency dispatch on the 3rd)

Japanese Ambassador Saito States Japan and the US Will Not Clash

I say this not as a diplomat, but as my personal honest opinion." Japan and the US have many common interests, and there are no major issues that would cause them to separate. Heavy Snowstorm in Japan: Only Seen Since Meiji Year 20

Transportation Disrupted, Damages Extremely Severe

Rough Seas Cause Ship Accidents

Tokyo - Since noon on the 4th, a heavy snowstorm suddenly began in Tokyo and other places, with the ground already covered in over a foot of snow. It became even more violent at night, and transportation was completely cut off. Incidents of collisions involving cars and streetcars occurred frequently, and order was extremely chaotic. This heavy snow is a new record since Meiji Year 20, and the damage is very severe. The Tokyo Municipal Electric Railway has ordered the emergency recruitment of 20,000 workers and 2,000 freight cars by dawn on the 5th in preparation for snow removal work. If it continues to snow at dawn on the 5th, then all government offices and bank personnel in the city will have concerns about being unable to move. (Dohmei News Agency dispatch on the 4th)

Yokohama - The area suddenly experienced a strong gale with wind speeds of 15 meters per second, coupled with heavy snow. Traffic order in the city was extremely chaotic. Countless large and small ships inside and outside the port were unable to move forward or backward. Numerous small boats were sunk, and the raging waves in the harbor were extremely dangerous. (Dohmei News Agency dispatch on the 4th)

Osaka - The unprecedented snowstorm blew off roofs and signs, and the number of houses collapsing and power poles breaking was also very high. Flooding occurred in the port area and along Sanjo Avenue, and residents rushed to evacuate. Ships in the Kobe harbor area were on special alert, and many private and fishing boats were also sunk. (Dohmei News Agency dispatch on the 4th)

Moji - Moji was hit by a severe snowstorm, and the waves at sea were huge, causing all ships to stop leaving port, resulting in considerable chaos. Connecting ferries were also temporarily suspended due to insufficient cargo. (Dohmei News Agency dispatch on the 4th)

Severe Cold in the Eastern US: Almost Entirely a World of Ice

The Hudson River Also Freezes

New York - The climate in the Eastern United States has been severely cold recently. The waters around Tangier Island off the coast of Virginia are surrounded by ice. The Hudson River in New York State has also frozen, causing the port of New York to be filled with huge ice floes, extending west along the coast to the Washington Bridge. According to a ship captain, his ship saw ice floes drifting near the coast when entering the harbor. In addition, Nantucket Island off the coast of Massachusetts, ten kilometers from the coast, is also trapped by ice, and communication between the island and the mainland is completely cut off. The 3,300 residents of the island used to receive bread daily by ship from the mainland, but due to the blockage of traffic, the source has been cut off. Although there are two bakers on the island, it is difficult to supply the needs of the entire island's residents, so there is a great risk of food shortage on the island. The authorities have dispatched an aircraft carrying 700 kilograms of food to the island to provide relief. (Havas dispatch on the 3rd)

US Agricultural Production Control: Three Bills Requested to Be Repealed

Roosevelt Message to Congress

Washington - President Roosevelt, in his message to Congress today, advocated the speedy repeal of the Bankhead Cotton Control Act, the Kerr-Smith Tobacco Act, and the 1935 Potato Act. The message was very short, stating that the agricultural adjustment program has ended, and these three acts are all its accessories, so he has this proposal. People in Washington were greatly shocked by this news, and political leaders felt it was strange, but they felt that this proposal may be related to the government's efforts to develop a new rural relief plan to replace the illegal AAA. The lawsuit filed by the Governor of Georgia alleging the illegality of the Bankhead Cotton Control Act will continue to be heard by the Supreme Court tomorrow, where the government will present its reasons for requesting the dismissal of the lawsuit. (Reuters dispatch on the 3rd)

Washington - Senator Smith today proposed in the Senate to clear government-owned cotton stocks. His proposed method stipulates that a maximum of 25,000 bales and a minimum of 15,000 bales be sold each week. The President has the right to appoint three people to oversee the clearing of cotton stocks. (Reuters dispatch on the 3rd)

Alternative to Agricultural Adjustment Act Passed by House Agriculture Committee

Washington - The House Agriculture Committee today passed the alternative to the Agricultural Adjustment Act. The bill had been delayed for several weeks due to legal issues and was finally passed today by a vote of 17 to 6. (National Telegraph Agency dispatch on the 3rd)

Treasury Approves Supplemental Budget

Washington - The Treasury Department today approved a supplemental budget of $367,700,000, of which $296,185,000 is for subsidies paid to farmers across the country, that is, the contracts signed by the government and farmers before the Agricultural Adjustment Act became invalid. (National Telegraph on the 3rd)

Washington - The faction in Congress advocating currency inflation through the Agricultural Mortgage Refinancing Act has suddenly changed its plan and reached a tacit understanding with the faction advocating for veteran bonuses. Therefore, the huge sum of $2,237,000,000 required for the veteran bonus bill was quickly passed today. The agricultural faction's sudden change of plan is due to the veteran bonus faction's opposition to attaching an inflationary clause to the veteran bonus bill. At the same time, it is known that the agricultural bill needs only three more signatures to force a congressional vote. The faction hopes that the veteran bonus inflation faction led by Patman will soon provide support. Currently, the inflation faction plans to temporarily suspend the movement to issue more banknotes to await President Roosevelt's submission of a new tax bill. (National Telegraph on the 3rd)

US Gold Reverse Flow: Using This to Maintain the Dollar's Status

Fears of Currency Inflation Dispelled

Washington - The US Treasury Department today approved the shipment of $5,240,000 in cash to France and $365,000 to the Netherlands. At the same time, the US dollar was greatly depreciated in the foreign exchange market. Treasury officials stated that if the dollar falls below the gold export point in the future, they will issue permits at any time to ship cash to gold standard countries. Cash has been flowing into the US for several months, causing the US gold reserves to break all records. Today's outflow is the first reverse flow decision. Officials are unwilling to comment on this matter, but some people have stated that they believe this trend is actually a good development because on the one hand, it can assist other countries' cash reserves, and at the same time, it can reduce the tendency of domestic credit inflation. (National Telegraph Agency dispatch on the 3rd)

New York - According to the report issued today by the Federal Reserve Bank of New York, cash worth US$5.6 million has been shipped to France from the bank's vault. From this point of view, it seems that the direction of cash flow has reversed in recent months. It is said that the Treasury Department approved the outflow of cash, apparently because this can maintain the status of the US dollar and dispel European concerns about US currency inflation. (National Telegraph Agency dispatch on the 3rd)

Washington - Treasury Secretary Morgenthau confirmed to reporters the claim that the United States is releasing gold to Europe, but only said that the US Treasury is prepared to allow gold to continue to be shipped out while exercising the current foreign exchange system. Other than that, he would not make any further remarks. (Reuters dispatch on the 3rd)

Washington - President Roosevelt today ordered the appointment of Eccles, President of the Federal Reserve Bank, as Chairman of the Federal Reserve Board. (National Telegraph Agency dispatch on the 3rd)

Effective from March 2nd

Washington - Another reciprocal trade agreement negotiated by the State Department under President Roosevelt's trade policy was announced today, as announced by the President, the United States and Honduras have signed this agreement. The agreement will take effect on March 2nd of this year. (National Telegraph Agency dispatch on the 3rd)

Dutch Bank Reduces Discount Rate

London - The interest rate of the Dutch Bank was reduced to 2.5% today, restoring the standard of April 1935. Since the end of September last year, financial matters have gradually improved due to the increase in interest rates to 6%. Of the 137,000,000 florins lost in the previous six months, 133,000,000 florins have been successively recovered by the Dutch Bank. However, although the status of the Dutch currency has improved, the Dutch budget is still unsatisfactory and in a deficit situation, leading many parties to believe that the Netherlands will eventually be forced to abandon the gold standard it upholds. However, it is heard that gold-using countries are now showing signs of recovery because the price difference between gold-using countries and currency-devaluing countries is now not very large. (Reuters dispatch on the 3rd)

Tokyo - The Chinese Export Company's ship Jiaxing (5658 tons) ran aground on a reef near the Miho no Matsubara lighthouse on its way from Dalian to Shimizu Port, Japan at noon on the 4th due to heavy snow. (Dohmei News Agency dispatch on the 4th)

February 4th, Reuters Special Commercial Report

Gold and Silver

London Premium: Today is 140 shillings and 6 pence, down 5 pence.

London Bar Silver: Today is stable, spot price is 19.75 pence, down 0.0625. India bought in, but the transaction was very small.

Montri Bar Silver Market Transaction: Today is sluggish, the opening price for March futures fell 15 pounds, to 44.40-45.00.

Exchange Rate

British-American: The dollar strengthened in the London foreign exchange market this morning. At 10:30, the British-American exchange rate was 5.028125 yuan, 5625 yuan lower than yesterday's closing price. It fell to 5.023125 yuan an hour later, but rose 25 yuan at 1:00 pm, to 5.025625 yuan.

Cotton and Wheat

US Cotton: The New York cotton market is becoming increasingly weak due to uncertainty regarding legislative events. The opening price for May futures was 10.88, 11 pounds lower than yesterday's closing price, and there was still a downward trend.

British Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market was more loose today. The March futures fell 875 at 1:00 pm, to 6 shillings and 3 pence.

British Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market fell 3 pounds at 1:00 pm today, with the May futures price at 5.78.

US Wheat: The Chicago wheat market was stable today, as were miscellaneous grains. The wheat price rose 125 at 11:00, to 99.625, and miscellaneous grains also rose 125, to 60.5.

Rubber

London: Rubber was stable today. At 1:00 pm, the April-June futures price was 7.125 pence, the same as yesterday.

New York: The rubber market was sluggish. Merchants were reluctant to buy more, so the price fluctuated very little. The opening price fell 12 pounds, and there was not much change afterwards.

Securities

New York: The stock market fell today due to profit-taking and multi-party closing. The opening prices of various securities were lower than yesterday's closing prices. The only ones that remained stable were department store stocks, railroad stocks, and steel stocks. Communication and automobile stocks fell 1.125, to 59.25.

Britain Takes the Offensive (Part 2)

— By Louis Fisher, translated by Bin Fu

——One of the Observations on the European Situation Under the Shadow of Slaughter——

Due to the Walwal border incident and Selassie's appeal to Geneva, the Abyssinian question has been fully embraced by the League of Nations, which London is determined to uphold. This is why Baldwin's government has gained domestic support. The large number of peace votes in the country shows how deep and pure the British people's desire for collective security is. It has also gained international support, as all countries fear that the success of aggression will drag Europe into a second great war. If an agreement had been concluded behind the League of Nations in Paris or elsewhere, Geneva might have softened, and Britain's naval demonstrations might not have amounted to much. The British fleet stationed in the Mediterranean has quickly increased from 230,000 tons on August 5, 1935, to 500,000 tons. Since 1918, Britain has never taken such decisive action. This is a natural result of the arms embargo, financial blockade, and economic sanctions decided by the League of Nations in September and October.

The speed and unanimity with which League and non-League members participated in the sanctions reflect Italy's moral isolation and material weakness, as well as Britain's unwavering determination. It may be easier for a powerful aggressor to deal with a small country than with Geneva. Therefore, sanctions are indeed a good method with many moral components. Although slow, this method is strict and universal, and does not lead to actual retaliation. It certainly cannot immediately stop the war, but it can limit the daily military consumption that accelerates the crisis. Not long ago, in Geneva, Paris, and London, I heard many people discussing whether sanctions should continue if Mussolini's or the Fascists' position in Italy was in danger. Sanctions can naturally be withdrawn immediately. But the biggest question is: what does Britain intend to do? Rumors of "despicable plans" to sacrifice Abyssinia can be heard every day. One moment, the British ambassador meets the Blackshirt leader in Rome; the next, Laval convenes talks on the Abyssinian issue. All the widespread plans aim to give Italy some satisfaction. Didn't former British Foreign Secretary Hoare say, "We are not without sympathy for Italy's need for expansion"? He also advocated for the redistribution of world raw materials.

Why is British policy so hesitant? There are many reasons, but they can all be summarized into one area. Britain's powerful circles do not want Mussolini to collapse; they are thinking about the future of European capitalism. Britain may still need Italy's help to resist France and Germany. An Italy that has been sanctioned or defeated may obediently abandon its conspiracies against the British Empire and its ambitions to seize Africa. Therefore, giving Italy a little land poses no danger to Great Britain, and it can also be used to dispel Anglo-Italian hostility. However, what if Italy, defying British mediation, joins hands with Germany and plunges all of Europe into war? This is certainly not what Britain wants. They must not push Mussolini to the point where there is no room for mediation. British armament expansionists certainly say that Mussolini's planes can destroy the British fleet. In fact, in addition to its existing strength, Britain also has the League of Nations as its backing, which is more than enough to deal with Italy. Britain's difficulty lies in the fact that she has three fronts—the Far East, the Mediterranean, and the North Sea or Central Europe. She really needs three navies. When London mobilizes on the Mediterranean front, the other two fronts must also remain active. This is another major factor in Britain's fundamental weakness. Britain's strength has been diverted by Japan's invasion of China or Germany's recent threats, which is a greater help to Mussolini. This is why the British government, in the Italo-Ethiopian dispute, wants to compromise with France or Germany at the expense of the League of Nations. Of the two, the military cooperation between Britain and France is probably the most likely, and this issue is now once again in the ascendant.

Today's war in East Africa cannot but remind people of the Fashoda Incident. Around the time of the Fashoda Incident, British Colonial Secretary Joseph Chamberlain wanted to ally with Germany, but Germany ignored him. In the spring of 1899, just before Britain and France resolved the Sudan issue, France asked Germany for an alliance, but Germany again ignored him. Soon, Britain and France concluded an agreement to contain Germany. Now, as a result of the Anglo-Italian contradiction, another kind of combination or conflict may arise. Nothing is more volatile than this. The colonial war in East Africa is setting the stage for the second act of the European drama.

It is also very clear that Britain's isolation, whether glorious or despicable, has come to an end. Only a very strong Britain can stand alone. The choice between the Empire and the Continent has become pure nonsense. There can be no Empire without Britain's power on the Continent. Every disputed border, every potential powder keg, is Britain's business, and the new Conservative cabinet should take this into account. Britain needs friends, and Britain should also build a larger air fleet and a sophisticated navy. Until it is built, she should avoid exposing weaknesses. Peace-lovers believe that collective security has been guaranteed, and that the League of Nations can reduce Britain's military budget. However, Downing Street knows the value of Geneva. It also knows that in today's chaotic world, the ultimate guarantee still lies in strength. In Europe, the arms race and Britain's power struggle are only just beginning.

The Opium Suppression Conference Concludes

Nanjing: The general assembly of the Opium Suppression Commission was held on the afternoon of the 4th. Twenty-three people, including Wu Dingchang, were in attendance. Jiao Qun and Li Zhonggong served as chairmen for the morning and afternoon sessions, respectively. Thirty-five important cases were passed, and the meeting concluded at 5 PM. At 6 PM, Chief Supervisor Jiang hosted a banquet for informal discussions and provided instructions on future opium suppression administration. Important cases resolved by each group included: Legal System Group: Establishing an Opium Suppression Law Compilation Committee; Establishing the highest administrative organ for opium suppression; Revising the criminal penalties for prohibited opium paraphernalia; Formulating regulations for investigating and verifying opium use among Party, government, military service personnel, and school staff and students. Opium Suppression Administration Group: Establishing drug rehabilitation hospitals; Sending letters to the Central Party Headquarters and the Ministry of Education to promote public anti-drug campaigns and anti-drug education and opium suppression publicity; Training opium suppression cadre personnel. Drug Prohibition Group: Sending a letter to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to handle opium prohibition in concessions; Sending a letter to the Executive Yuan to instruct various ministries to formulate measures for the import of coffee, sugar, and lactose; Using the joint liability method to prohibit opium cultivation, consumption, transportation, and sale. Regarding the group: The Chief Supervisor is to send a circular telegram to the provincial and municipal governments, holding them responsible for registering, investigating, and reporting opium addicts; Reporting opium use among Party, government, and military service personnel and school staff and students; The Chief Supervisor is to send a letter to various ministries and commissions to jointly handle the rehabilitation of overseas laborers who use opium; Strictly prohibiting poppy seeds. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 4th)

Chen Guangfu Authors Article Discussing China's New Monetary Policy

Paris: Chen Guangfu, General Manager of the Shanghai Commercial and Savings Bank of China, Chinese Director of the Shanghai Public Concession, and Chairman of the Chinese National Committee of the International Chamber of Commerce, recently published an article in the journal "International Economics" discussing the new monetary policy promulgated by the Chinese government on November 4 of last year and referring to it as a step in the process of international monetary stabilization. Chen first described the process by which the Chinese government implemented the new monetary policy, stating that China was originally a silver standard country, and 95% of its foreign trade was conducted with gold standard countries or countries that controlled currency and therefore had stable currencies. China had encountered various difficulties in stabilizing its currency. Since the U.S. government implemented the Silver Purchase Act, its impact on the Chinese economy had been truly negative, eventually leading to an unprecedented panic. The Chinese government therefore implemented the new monetary policy on November 4 of last year and decided to establish a Central Reserve Bank to secure a 60% hard currency reserve for the paper currency it had issued or would issue, so as to achieve the maximum degree of stability for the Chinese currency. Chen concluded, "China's new monetary policy should not cause any anxiety. All rational people should fully support it. The Chinese government is doing this to stabilize the currency, with no other intention. The promotion of international trade depends on whether the currency can be stabilized. It can be seen that the implementation of China's new monetary policy will not only benefit China but also all countries that trade with China." In short, the current panic in China's foreign trade has greatly improved as a result, and the path to the ultimate stabilization of international currency has also been opened. The stabilization of international currency is what the International Chamber of Commerce has always advocated and what I personally sincerely pray for. (Havas dispatch from the 3rd)

Impressions of Traveling North: By Our Special Correspondent, Geng Ya

9. The Strengthening of Eastern Hebei and Northern Chahar:

Since the September 18th Incident, Japan's ambitions have grown increasingly fierce. In order to thoroughly implement its continental policy, it has adopted a strategy of gradual advancement and aggression, encroaching westward and southward. Towards the end of the year, in our northern provinces, problems related to "Eastern Hebei," "Northern Chahar," and "Eastern Suiyuan" were created one after another. The Hebei-Chahar Political Council, which emerged in response to these issues, had fantastical dreams of negotiating the Eastern Hebei and Northern Chahar problems. However, after two months of negotiations, there was no progress whatsoever. Furthermore, as the situations in "Eastern Hebei" and "Northern Chahar" became established facts, their influence grew, and the strength of the Hebei-Chahar authorities was gradually weakened, becoming like "a clay Buddha crossing the river, barely able to save itself."

When Yin Rugeng reorganized the puppet "Eastern Hebei Anti-Communist Autonomous Government," in his absurd and reckless declaration, he first admitted that "the advocacy of autonomy has been going on for a month, but many prominent figures are still hesitant to support it." At the end, he shamelessly boasted, "By rectifying governance and strengthening ourselves with vigilance, we can solidify Eastern Hebei's autonomy like a rock and usher in a new opportunity for national restoration." In his conversations with visiting reporters, he also made the preposterous claim that he would govern Eastern Hebei as a model zone, and then promote it throughout North China and the entire nation.

The Eastern Hebei war zone, which originally had the First, Second, Third, Fourth, and Fifth Security Regiments, has been reorganized into official troops directly under the puppet government. They have been given new uniforms and insignias, and are now called the First, Second, Third, Fourth, and Fifth Divisions. The Japanese Kwantung Army, pleased that Yin Rugeng had so skillfully carried out their intentions, greatly appreciated him, stating that if Yin Rugeng had been in Li Jichun's position in Eastern Hebei earlier, today's achievements would have been even greater. Therefore, they are now making every effort to supplement the military strength of the Eastern Hebei puppet organization.

There are 200 Japanese troops stationed at the Tong County Normal School, serving as a powerful bodyguard for the puppet organization's location. In the 22 counties of Eastern Hebei, the textbooks used in schools are being revised under the guise of "thoroughly eliminating Kuomintang education," but in reality, their intention is no different from promoting the enslaved textbooks currently used in the puppet "Manchukuo."

The Hebei-Chahar Political Council intends to invite Yin Rugeng to join as a member, or even concurrently serve as the head of Tianjin. However, Yin Rugeng still claims that the establishment of the puppet organization is not for personal power, and that anyone with the same goals can cooperate, but that he cannot discuss personal matters. It is clear that the Eastern Hebei problem will be difficult to resolve through peaceful means. A single spark can start a prairie fire, and the future hidden dangers are countless, needless to say.

As for "Northern Chahar" and "Eastern Suiyuan" in relation to "Eastern Hebei," there was originally a three-in-one connection. Initially, Li Shouxin's troops from the puppet "Manchukuo" occupied the Six Banners of Northern Chahar. Subsequently, the Mongolian security forces under Zhuo Shihai declared independence. It can be said that the Japanese are already in the preliminary stages of successfully creating an "Independent Inner Mongolia." The situation in Eastern Suiyuan has become increasingly serious around the Spring Festival. However, this area is not under the Hebei-Chahar Pacification Zone but under the Shanxi-Suiyuan Pacification Zone. The willingness and ability of the Shanxi-Suiyuan authorities to deal with the situation may differ from those of Hebei-Chahar. As the saying goes, "Pull one hair and the whole body moves." The new developments in Eastern Suiyuan are therefore noteworthy.

The Japanese and their puppets have two aims in their westward encroachment on Chahar and Suiyuan. One is to threaten Outer Mongolia from the north and copy the Soviet Russian Siberian Railway. The other is to control Inner Mongolia, connect the Ping-Sui Railway with the Bei-Ning and South Manchurian Railways, and use other forms of aggression, such as so-called "economic development" and "technical cooperation" strategies. They plan to extend the Ping-Sui Railway, pass through the Hetao region, and turn towards Ningxia, then follow the natural barrier of the Wei River and Yellow River to encircle and divide the entire land north of the Yellow River.

Furthermore, this contains an important significance: to cut off China's transportation with Outer Mongolia and Soviet Russia. According to reliable sources, the Japanese side intends to present the plan to extend the Ping-Sui Railway to the relevant parties once the situation in North China has been further stabilized. They hope for... (the end of this sentence is cut off)

The Evolution of 33 Types of Old Bonds

—All to be Exchanged for Unified Public Bonds—

In February of the 21st year of the Republic (1932), due to decreased tax revenue and a sluggish bond market, the Ministry of Finance and various groups held extensive discussions to re-draft appropriate standards for the originally promulgated public bond regulations. It was also decided that 8.6 million yuan would be allocated monthly from customs duties as a fund for repaying various bonds, with an annual interest rate of six percent and an adjusted repayment period.

Over the past few years, the severity of the national crisis has not diminished. Internally, we have suffered frequent natural disasters and banditry. Externally, we have been affected by global economic panic, coupled with the impact of rising silver prices. Government tax revenues of all kinds have decreased, and the shortfall in customs duties allocated to the bond principal and interest fund has been particularly significant. However, the government has consistently paid principal and interest on time and has never defaulted. The government's painstaking efforts to maintain this in the midst of immense financial difficulties are well known both at home and abroad.

However, due to the recent shortfall in customs revenue, the financial situation has become more difficult, which will affect various bond funds. In light of this severe situation, Finance Minister Kong Xiangxi, in order to revive the economy, stabilize finances, and maintain the credit of the bonds, consulted with the financial community and decided to issue unified public bonds to exchange for old bonds, and to issue revival public bonds to improve the health of the financial system. The Bondholders' Association has also issued a declaration supporting this move. The following is a summary of the evolution of the old bonds:

Type A Bonds to be Cleared in 12 Years

A total of six types: 1. Patriotic Treasury Bills of the 22nd year of the Republic (1933), with a bond amount of 20 million yuan, a monthly interest rate of five percent, and principal and interest paid at the end of each month, to be fully repaid by November of the 25th year of the Republic (1936). As of the end of January this year, the total principal outstanding is 4,741,848.81 yuan. 2. Customs Treasury Bills of the 18th year of the Republic (1929), with a bond amount of 40 million yuan, a monthly interest rate of seven percent, reduced to five percent in the 21st year of the Republic (1932), originally scheduled to be fully repaid by the end of July of the 23rd year of the Republic (1934). The new bond schedule revised in February of the 21st year of the Republic (1932) still stipulated monthly repayments of principal and interest, but the repayment period was extended to July of the 26th year of the Republic (1937). As of the end of January this year, the total principal outstanding is 7,861,505.82 yuan. 3. North China Public Bonds of the 22nd year of the Republic (1933), with a bond amount of 4 million yuan and an annual interest rate of six percent, to be repaid by the end of July of the 27th year of the Republic (1938). As of the end of January this year, the total principal outstanding is 2,200,000 yuan. 4. Customs Bonds of the 19th year of the Republic (1930), with a bond amount of 80 million yuan, a monthly interest rate of eight percent, reduced to five percent in the 21st year of the Republic (1932), originally scheduled to be fully repaid by May of the 24th year of the Republic (1935). The new bond schedule revised in February of the 21st year of the Republic (1932) still stipulated monthly repayments of principal and interest, but the repayment period was extended to January of the 28th year of the Republic (1939). As of the end of January this year, the total principal outstanding is 32,960,000 yuan. 5. Short-Term Treasury Certificates, details unknown. 6. Security Bonds, with a bond amount of 2 million yuan and an annual interest rate of eight percent, reduced to six percent in the 21st year of the Republic (1932). Starting from February of the 21st year of the Republic (1932), it was revised so that interest was paid only in the first four years, once each on the 10th of January, April, July, and October each year. From the fifth year onwards, principal and interest were repaid once each on the 10th of January, April, July, and October each year, originally scheduled to be fully repaid by January of the 28th year of the Republic (1939). As of the end of January this year, the total principal outstanding is 2,000,000 yuan.

The new bond schedule revised in February of the 21st year of the Republic (1932) still stipulated monthly repayments of principal and interest, but the repayment period was extended to January of the 30th year of the Republic (1941).
