The Murderer of a Young Woman Sends Another Letter: Over a Thousand Words in Tiny Script, Claiming Jealousy and Revenge for Unrequited Love

On the first of this month, in room number 54 of the Anshang Hotel at 37 Baliao Bridge Street in the French Concession, a young married woman named Zhu, a guest at the hotel, was murdered by a man who identified himself as Zhao Junming. The murderer left a letter and fled, and the crime was discovered by a tea server named Chen Jinyu. He reported it to the French police, who dispatched detectives to investigate. The body was taken to the coroner's office for examination. The Second Special District Court sent officials to confirm the death. Because no relatives came to identify the body, it was entrusted to the Tongren Fuyuantang for preparation and burial. The French police issued orders to all detectives to investigate and apprehend the fugitive murderer. The gist of the murderer's letter was reported in this newspaper three times already. It is now learned that the Anshang Hotel received another letter from the murderer, delivered by the post office, at 6 PM on the afternoon of the third. Upon opening the letter, it was found to contain ten sheets of scattered paper, filled with over a thousand words in tiny script, detailing his relationship with the deceased and his feelings of anger that led him to lure and kill her in revenge. The main points are similar to the previous letter, but this one also includes details of his relationship and love with the deceased. He had intended to marry her and had even initiated divorce proceedings with his own wife. However, after the lawsuit was settled and the divorce finalized, the deceased became unfaithful and found a new lover, refusing to marry him. This not only cost him several thousand dollars but also left him feeling despondent and without any interest in life. Therefore, he lured and killed her in revenge. He claimed to have seen through the world and intended to retreat to the mountains to cultivate his spirituality. He also instructed the hotel to dress the deceased in her clothes and asked them to sell her two gold rings to purchase a simple coffin for her burial. He warned that if they did not comply with his instructions or if anyone tried to profit from the situation, they would be treated in the same way as the deceased. He also mentioned that the deceased's new lover was currently in Wuxi. After reading the letter, the hotel accountant immediately sent it to the French police for investigation. Furthermore, in his previous letter, the murderer stated that the deceased's real name was Zhang Fuying. It is now learned that the police found a gold ring among the deceased's belongings with the name "Fuying" engraved on it, while the other ring was made of copper. Based on this, it is believed that the deceased's name was indeed Zhang Fuying, and it is likely that she was from Wuxi. The police have already inventoried the deceased's belongings, including her clothes and gold rings, and sent them to the court archives the day before yesterday to await identification by her relatives.

A Gambling Dispute Leads to Murder in Sanlintang, Pudong: Gangsters Demand Extortion Money, Then Seek Revenge with a Mob, Killing a Teahouse Patron Named Cao Genfa

—The Teahouse Owner’s Daughter is Unjustly Injured—

In a teahouse opened by Chen Zhanglin in Tianhua'an Township, east of Sanlintang, Pudong, illegal gambling had been taking place since the beginning of the lunar new year, with high spirits and significant winnings and losses. On the seventh day of the lunar new year, a gangster from Zhoupu Township suddenly arrived at the teahouse and attempted to extort money from Chen Zhanglin, who refused. Enraged and humiliated, the gangster forcibly seized money from the gambling table. Chen, seeing this, became furious and shouted for help. The gamblers rushed forward and beat the gangster. Realizing he was outnumbered, the gangster fled in a disheveled state. However, he remained bitter after being beaten and gathered forty to fifty of his cronies a few days ago to seek revenge. They took a small train to the east station of Tianhua'an, armed with axes, iron rulers, and other weapons. They stormed into the teahouse and attacked anyone they encountered, destroying everything in sight. Fortunately, Chen Zhanglin had heard rumors and had already hidden himself, avoiding harm. However, Cao Genfa, a patron (37 years old, a native of the area, residing in Caojiazhai, about three li northeast of Tianhua'an, and a sawyer by trade), was caught in the chaos and was struck in the head by an axe, causing him to bleed profusely. The other patrons scattered and fled. Frustrated that they had not found Chen Zhanglin, the gang left in a hurry. They then encountered Wang, the 25-year-old daughter of the teahouse owner, and, suspecting she was related to Chen Zhanglin, they also struck her in the left shoulder with an axe. The gangsters then left on the small train. Afterwards, Wang was taken to the Sanlintang Hospital for treatment. Cao Genfa was helped home, but his injuries were too severe, and he died the next day. The local bailiff reported the incident to the local court prosecutor's office, requesting an autopsy. The court, upon receiving the report, dispatched Prosecutor Lei Binzhang and Coroner Shen Qixiu across the river yesterday morning to Cao's residence. They confirmed that the deceased, Cao Genfa, had suffered numerous axe wounds to the head, damaging his skull, which was the cause of death. A coroner's report was filled out, and the widow and others filed a case, requesting justice. The judge agreed to apprehend the murderers and investigate the matter.

A Strangled Female Corpse Discovered in a Field on Huangxing Road: Body Moved and Abandoned After Death, Small Round Mirror Found Nearby

Yesterday morning, a female corpse, strangled to death, was discovered in a field near Huangxing Road in Yinxianggang. The local bailiff, Lu Guisheng, reported it to the local court prosecutor's office, requesting an examination. In the afternoon, Prosecutor Li Fen and Coroner Shen arrived at the scene. They determined that the female corpse was approximately 30 years old. She was wearing a gray silk cheongsam, lined with a black cloth jacket and trousers, black cloth shoes, and gray cotton socks. Her hair was cut short. A small round mirror and several copper coins were found near her. A gray cloth leg binding was wrapped around her neck, indicating that she had been strangled. It was observed that the silk fabric on the back of her cheongsam, around the buttocks, was completely torn, suggesting that she had been murdered elsewhere and her body dragged and abandoned there, causing the damage to her clothing. Since no family members came forward to identify her, it was ordered that the body be taken to the Shantang (a charitable organization) for preparation and burial. The small round mirror was taken back to the archives for safekeeping.

The Liquidator of the Guang Sheng Li Leather Factory Discovers Altered Accounting Books: Suspected of Destroying Evidence, Additional Security Deposit of 10,000 Yuan Required

The Guang Sheng Li Leather Factory, located at 368 Tiantong Road, declared liquidation in June of the 21st year of the Republic (1932) due to the impact of the January 28th Shanghai Incident. Guangdong native Deng Zhongze and lawyer Wang Siji were appointed to establish a liquidation office at 10 Daqing Li, Nanjing Road (Deng's residence). Deng was accused by shareholder He Jinlin in a report from lawyer Wang, filed on December 31st of last year, of embezzling a significant amount of funds. The most obvious instance was the embezzlement of 4,500 yuan. On January 27th of this year, the Hongkou Police Department was notified and dispatched Chinese Detective Zhu Jihuang to secretly apprehend Deng at his address and escort him to the First Special District Court for questioning. Details of the interrogation have been reported in this newspaper. Deng provided a security deposit of 10,000 yuan, and the police department investigated the factory's accounting books and scheduled another hearing. Yesterday morning, Judge Xiao Bianfen continued the hearing at the Third Criminal Court. Labor Bureau lawyer Zhang Shizhu stated that examining the factory's various accounting books during the adjournment had been difficult. The defendant had used evasive language and claimed to be mentally fatigued to the police. The accuser's side questioned Song Zhenchu, the accountant of the liquidation office, who testified that Deng had instructed him to transcribe two new sets of accounting books at the end of last month, transferring all expenses and other costs from one ledger. These items were not recorded in the old books, which Deng then hid. It has now been discovered that Deng embezzled over 20,000 yuan, possibly more, and a detailed investigation is still required. The defendant intentionally destroyed evidence, which is a serious offense. A further adjournment and an increased security deposit were requested, and it was requested that the defendant not be allowed to leave Shanghai. The two new accounting books were presented for inspection. Accountant Song Zhenchu then testified about Deng's instructions to transcribe the two new accounting books. The lawyer stated that his law firm rented the western wing of the lower floor of the Daqing Li liquidation office building, which was owned by Deng's second wife. The Guang Sheng Li liquidation office was later established there. The rent was 30 yuan, and it was paid by the liquidation office from October of the 22nd year of the Republic (1933) onwards; previously, he had been responsible for it. The two new accounting books had not been seen before, and the various expenses and costs were inconsistent. When questioned, the defendant was evasive. Lawyer Yan Xujie defended him. Judge Xiao ordered Deng Zhongze to provide an additional security deposit of 10,000 yuan, to be available for questioning at any time, and not to leave his original residence.

Fire on Huaxing Road: An Elderly Woman Burned to Death, The Victim Was 75 Years Old

A fire broke out at a residence at number 54 Huaxing Road, west of the Zhabei Hanqiao, belonging to a Taoist surnamed Mou, at 3:05 PM yesterday. Thick smoke billowed out, and flames spread rapidly, engulfing the adjacent houses at numbers 52 and 56. New Silver-Nickel-Copper Subsidiary Coins to Circulate on March 1st: Simultaneously Used in Cities such as Beijing, Shanghai, and Wuhan, New Coin Fineness Already Extracted and Chemically Tested

In order to unify the value of subsidiary coins, the Ministry of Finance ordered the Central Mint to begin minting new silver-nickel-copper subsidiary coins at the end of last year. By the end of last month, a large number of coins had been accumulated, totaling tens of millions. To ensure that the coins met the fineness standards of the new subsidiary coin law, the mint had Chemical Tester Ge Laide extract and chemically test the coins in accordance with the fineness standards issued by the Ministry of Finance. According to inquiries from a Xin Xin News Agency reporter, the Ministry of Finance has determined that the coins are urgently needed in various regions and has decided to begin circulating them on March 1st. It has also been decided to first distribute them to the central bank branches in provinces such as Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Fujian, Jiangxi, Hunan, Hubei, and Anhui for exchange. At that time, the Ministry of Finance will issue a public announcement. After the second batch of coins is minted in larger quantities, they will be distributed to other provinces for circulation. The reorganization and reminting of old subsidiary coins such as silver dimes and copper coins will be decided by the Subsidiary Coin Committee after further study.

Chauffeur Accused of Secretly Selling Narcotics: Conflicting Testimony, Court Adjourns for Sentencing

Li Kuiyuan, a native of Qingjiang who works as a chauffeur, was stopped by Chinese detective Xu Dezhong from the Laozha Police Department and Chinese and Western police officers at the intersection of Guangxi Road and Jiujiang Road at 10:45 PM on the 27th of last month. A packet of heroin was found in his car. He stated that the heroin belonged to Wang Yongqing, his landlord at number 9 Wujialong, Huanlong Road, who asked him to sell it. He was taken into custody by the First Special District Court. On the 28th of last month, Wang Yongqing suddenly surrendered himself to the Laozha Police Department, stating that according to Li Kuiyuan's wife, the heroin was found by their employed maid, Qiaoyun, and that Li was falsely accusing him. After investigation, the detectives determined that Wang's statement was untrue and summoned Wang to the police department for detention a few days ago. Yesterday morning, he was taken to the criminal court of the First Special District Court. The police department lawyer Chen Ming presented the case, stating that Li's wife, Yang, and the maid, Qiaoyun, were both present in court today and requested to be questioned. Judge Qian Hongye questioned Li Yang, Qiaoyun, Li Kuiyuan, and Wang Yongqing separately. Li Yang and Qiaoyun's testimonies were contradictory. They claimed both that Qiaoyun had found the heroin and that Wang Yongqing had instructed them to make that statement in order to exonerate himself. Li Kuiyuan insisted that Wang had asked him to sell it. Wang claimed that Li was falsely accusing him and that he had been working at the Hongen Hospital on Daxi Road for over ten years, had always been law-abiding, and would never do anything illegal. The police department's lawyer Wang stated that the car owner urgently needed the car, so the police department had approved a temporary loan and requested approval to return it. Judge Qian reviewed the testimonies and adjourned the case for sentencing. The two defendants were returned to custody. The outcome was very uncertain.

New Postal Steamer for the Post Office Successfully Completes Sea Trial: Launching Ceremony in Mid-Month

In order to facilitate postal transportation along the Huangpu River, the National Postal Administration of the Ministry of Communications commissioned the Jiangnan Shipyard to build a new type of fast, large postal steamer. The steamer has been completed and has already undergone sea trials. The steamer is named "Hongxin" and is 100 feet long, 18 feet wide, and 9 feet 3 inches deep. It has a displacement of 45 tons and a 400-horsepower engine. It can travel at 11.5 nautical miles per hour. The sea trials were successfully completed yesterday. The Postal Administration will soon send personnel to inspect and accept the vessel, and the official launching ceremony will be held in the middle of this month.

Wanted by the Court on Charges of Fraud and Damaging Creditor's Rights: Lingering Deposit Disputes with the Jinxing Real Estate Company, Defendant Cannot Be Summoned, Trial Suspended

Sun Chunsheng, the owner of the Jinxing Real Estate Company at 505 Henan Road, previously mortgaged 7 mu, 8 fen, 1 li, and 5 hao of land, along with buildings, at the Baokang Li base at the corner of Zhejiang Road and Beijing Road to the Hongsheng Fuji Money Exchange for 1.18 million yuan. A contract was signed stipulating that all rental income from the mortgaged property would be assigned to the Hongsheng Exchange from March 1st of last year and that no other lease agreements could be privately entered into. However, Sun failed to comply with the agreement, and the exchange sent a letter of demand on April 9th, which Sun did not contest. The exchange then filed a lawsuit to compel the assignment of rental income, and the First Special District Court and the Second Branch of the High Court both ruled in favor of the exchange. The Hongsheng Exchange obtained permission for provisional execution, but just as enforcement was about to begin, Sun colluded with the British Yexing Company, claiming that all rental income, amounting to approximately half of the actual rental income, had been leased to the company. Yexing then engaged the Murakami Law Firm to obstruct the execution. Hongsheng Exchange, believing that Sun was attempting to damage creditor's rights, engaged lawyers Cai Liuheng and Dong Chi to file a complaint with the criminal court of the First Special District Court, accusing Sun of fraud and damaging creditor's rights under Articles 356 and 339 of the Criminal Code, and requesting that he be punished accordingly. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Ye Shengchao of the Ninth Criminal Court of the First Special District Court opened the trial for questioning. However, the address listed for Sun Chunsheng by the plaintiff was 325 Huade Road, the intersection of Dalian Bay Road. Since the house had already been sealed by the court, the summons could not be delivered. The plaintiff's attorney stated that, apart from this address, the defendant's whereabouts were unknown. Judge Ye then ordered the trial to be suspended and a warrant issued for the arrest of the defendant Sun Chunsheng.

Sixth Mass Wedding: Held Today at 3 PM, Hall Decorations More Sumptuous Than Before, Secretary-General Yu Guided Rehearsals Yesterday

The sixth mass wedding in this city will be held at 3 PM today in the auditorium of the Municipal Government. There will be 97 couples. A rehearsal was held yesterday afternoon at 2 PM, guided by Municipal Government Secretary-General Yu Hongjun and Section Chief Zhang Binghui. Details are as follows:

More Sumptuous Hall Decorations

This year's wedding hall will be in the same location, the Municipal Government Auditorium. The decorations are similar to previous years, but more sumptuous and magnificent than previous sessions. In addition to the red decorations on the altar and the carpet in the center of the hall, enameled wedding couple numbers have been made and placed on both sides and in the center. Red silk banners hang on both sides of the hall. In front of the altar are a pair of large candles and five pairs of small candles. The large candles are inserted into a pair of newly made, dragon and phoenix candlesticks of tin alloy, weighing over 500 jin and valued at over 1,000 yuan. They are bright and dazzling. Eight pieces of Hunan embroidery hang on the walls of the hall. The materials are of high quality, and the embroidery is exquisite. The embroidered birds and beasts look lifelike from afar, adding to the hall's beauty.

Simple Ceremony Broadcast on the Radio

The wedding ceremony will be similar to previous sessions, simple and solemn. The ceremony will begin at 3 PM today, with 97 couples participating. The ceremony will consist of seven parts: All wedding participants stand at attention; The new couples offer their highest respects to the party and national flags and the portrait of Sun Yat-sen; The director of the Social Affairs Bureau reads the wedding certificate; The new couples bow to each other three times; The officiant issues wedding certificates and souvenirs, which the new couples accept in turn; The mayor gives a speech; The new couples bow to the officiant; The ceremony concludes. The ceremony will also be broadcast by the municipal radio station. The hall staff assigned are altar attendants Sun Yongyi and Yan Wenkai, master of ceremonies Shen Zuhui, and the leading new couples Zhang Binghui and his wife.

Successful Rehearsal Yesterday

Yesterday, in order to ensure uniformity during the ceremony today, the Municipal Government held a rehearsal of the entire wedding ceremony at 2 PM in the Municipal Government Auditorium. Mayor Wu and Social Affairs Bureau Director Wu were unable to attend due to official duties and sent Municipal Government Secretary-General Yu Hongjun and Social Affairs Bureau Section Chief Zhang Binghui as representatives to guide the rehearsal. At 2:35 PM, the wedding participants arrived and began the rehearsal. Secretary-General Yu first announced that guests should maintain order. Then, Municipal Social Affairs Bureau staff led the new couples from the lounge, along the front of the Municipal Government, and up the stone steps to the hall. The military band played music. The most important parts of the ceremony, such as the bowing of the new couples to each other, were rehearsed one by one. The rehearsal was very successful, with each couple performing the ceremony flawlessly according to the regulations. The order in the hall was quiet and uneventful, as it had never been during past rehearsals. At 3:40 PM, the rehearsal concluded. The band played music, and the new couples walked out of the hall in turn. They took a group photo in front of the Municipal Government. Then, the Social Affairs Bureau provided large cars to transport each wedding participant back home, and they dispersed.

Ministry of Industry, Ministry of Finance, and Ministry of Railways Award the Great China Double Coin Brand Automobile Tires

The Great China Rubber Factory was founded in the 17th year of the Republic (1928) and specializes in the manufacture of rubber boots and shoes and various rubber products. It has a total of eight factories and branches, with distribution offices in Shanghai, Beijing, Wuhan, Guangzhou, Chongqing, Wuhu, and Wenzhou. It employs approximately 3,000 workers. Daily output is limited to boots and shoes, with as many as 40,000 to 50,000 pairs produced. The majority of domestic military and police personnel use these products, so imported rubber shoes are now almost absent from the market. Recognizing the progress of domestic transportation construction, the factory has also focused on the manufacture of various vehicle tires. Automobile inner and outer tires, rickshaw inner and outer tires, and bicycle inner and outer tires were first shipped two years ago. Recently, the Ministry of Industry notified the factory that, because the factory's manufacture of automobile tires is the only domestic imitation of transportation equipment, it has been granted exclusive manufacturing rights in the Shanghai area for five years. The Ministry of Finance has approved an exemption from transit duties for three years, effective from February 1st. The Ministry of Railways has approved a reduction of one grade, to the third grade, for automobile tires in the newly added category 29 (industrial arts) of the freight classification table, for a period of two years. Recently, the Northwest National Railway Bureau, the Fujian Provincial Automobile Management Office, the Zhejiang Provincial Construction Department, the Transportation Corps, the Xicheng Long-Distance Bus Company, the Xihu Long-Distance Bus Company, and the Hutai Long-Distance Bus Company have all placed orders, as the factory's products are effective, safe, and comparable to the best imported products. If all highways and automobile companies can adopt these products, the government and the people will provide strong support for them, recovering a significant amount of lost revenue. In the future, this will also greatly assist in transportation and national defense.

Tan Fucai, a blind man, 33 years old, was walking through the entrance of Lane 384, Peikai'er Road, in Pudong yesterday morning at around 10 AM, when a truck, number 16771, belonging to the Maotai Transportation Company, struck him. Only One Silk Factory Currently Operating in This City

Most Factories Cannot Operate Due to Lack of Raw Materials

Silk Improvement Association Purchases Silkworm Eggs to Increase Production

Of the silk factories in this city, only one has resumed operations since the total accounting at the end of the lunar year. Two or three more are expected to resume operations in the coming days. In order to find ways to increase the production of silkworm cocoons, the Sericulture Improvement Committee of the National Economic Council has purchased a large number of silkworm eggs from Italy and Japan and transported them to Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces for distribution to silkworm farmers. Details are as follows, according to inquiries from a Dagong She reporter:

Only One Silk Factory Operating

Since the autumn of last year, a total of 43 silk factories in this city have been operating. However, due to a shortage of raw materials, they successively ceased operations only six months later. At the time of the total accounting for the 24th year of the Republic (1935), nine factories were still in operation, but all ceased operations during the closing period. As of yesterday, only the Jiyu Silk Factory on Gonghe Road has announced that it will resume operations. All other districts, such as Zhabei, Hunan, and Hongkou, have not resumed operations. A Dagong She reporter learned yesterday from the silk industry that the main reason why the silk factories cannot resume operations is the lack of raw materials. However, the Dongyi Factory in the Zhabei district, the Fulun Factory in the Hongkou district, and the Yihe Factory in the French Concession are expected to resume operations in the coming weeks. Other factories will only be able to resume operations in June, when spring silkworms appear on the market. Therefore, the maximum number of silk factories in this city that will resume operations in the spring is only four or five.

Purchasing Silkworm Eggs for Distribution and Cultivation

Because last year, all of the silk factories felt the lack of raw materials and successively stopped operations, the Sericulture Improvement Committee of the National Economic Council specially sent personnel to Italy and Japan in December of last year to purchase a large number of silkworm eggs for distribution to silkworm farmers in preparation for silkworm breeding when the spring silkworm season arrives. It is learned that 70,000 sheets of Japanese silkworm eggs have been purchased in Kobe and Osaka, totaling 700,000 grams. The brand names are "Hua Liu × Hua Gui" and "Hua Gui × Hua Liu". The price of each sheet, including transportation costs, is 8 jiao. However, in order to promote silkworm breeding among farmers, they are sold to farmers for 4 jiao per sheet. Italian silkworm eggs will also be transported to China in the coming days and then distributed by the committee to silkworm farmers in the two provinces for cultivation.

Central Bank Inspection Report

The 268th inspection report on the issuance reserve for Central Bank convertible banknotes states: In accordance with Article 13 of the Central Bank Law, this committee is responsible for inspecting the number of convertible banknotes issued by this bank and the reserve funds. The 268th inspection was conducted at the Issuance Bureau of this bank on February 1, 25th year of the Republic (1936). The results of the inspection are reported as follows: (A) The total amount of convertible banknotes issued is 224,838,507 silver dollars, including 203,134,777 silver dollar banknotes and 21,700,370 subsidiary currency banknotes. The total amount of convertible banknote reserve funds is 224,838,507 silver dollars, including 162,482,827 silver dollars in cash reserves. This cash reserve includes 106,391,707 yuan, 9 jiao and 4 fen stored in the bank's issuing headquarters, branches, and sub-branches, and 62,355,680 silver dollars in collateral reserves. (B) The total amount of Customs Gold convertible banknotes issued is 373,324.7 yuan. The total amount of Customs Gold convertible banknote reserve funds is 373,324.7 yuan. This reserve fund includes 7,351 liang, 9 qian, and 5 fen of standard gold, equivalent to 373,324.7 yuan of Customs Gold at a fixed price of 50779. In accordance with Article 22 of the Central Bank Law, the cash reserve must be at least 60%, and the remainder must be secured with legal collateral. The results of this inspection show that the cash reserve exceeds 60%, and the collateral reserve is within 40%, which is in accordance with the law. This report is hereby submitted. February 3, 25th year of the Republic of China. Central Bank Supervisory Committee Chairman Li Fusun. Supervisors Xie Mengjun, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, and Xu Jiyu.

Since the promulgation of the Traditional Chinese Medicine Ordinance, traditional Chinese medicine practitioners have gained legal status, and the number of people studying traditional Chinese medicine has increased. Shanghai's Cigarette Industry

— Compiled by China Credit Information

(Overview of Shanghai's Industry and Commerce, No. 12)

I. History The habit of smoking in our country is very old. In addition to opium, which is deeply poisonous, people have long known how to cut tobacco leaves into fine strands and use copper water pipes or bamboo dry pipes to smoke at will, which is quite troublesome. Therefore, since cigarettes were imported from abroad, their popularity has continued to expand. Today, almost every remote village has traces of cigarettes. This is because cigarettes have novel styles and are more convenient to carry and smoke than other types of tobacco.

The earliest import of cigarettes was around 1890 (i.e., 22 years before the founding of the Republic of China). The earliest business was the American firm Lao Jinlong. At that time, the annual value was only several hundred thousand yuan. Later, it increased year by year. In the sixth year of the Republic of China, it increased to more than 40 million yuan, which is truly shocking. At the same time, British and American merchants established branch factories of the British American Tobacco Company in Shanghai, Hankou, and other places ten years before the founding of the Republic of China to manufacture locally. Their momentum was even stronger. The rise of Chinese-run cigarette companies was very slow. It was not heard until about seven years before the founding of the Republic of China. At that time, because the United States banned Chinese workers from entering the country, the Chinese were greatly stimulated. In the cigarette industry, they also rose up to seek independence. Companies such as the Samsung Company and Delong Tobacco Factory in Shanghai, the Dazhong Company in Peiping, the Beiyang Company in Tianjin, and the Nanyang Company in Guangzhou were all stimulated by the American anti-Chinese wave at that time. However, due to insufficient capital and lack of experience, the Nanyang Company was reorganized in a few years, and the other factories closed down. Later, when the European War broke out, foreign goods could not be imported continuously, and Chinese tobacco factories were able to take the opportunity to become active. After the May 30th Incident, anti-British sentiment was very strong throughout the country, and Chinese tobacco factories sprung up like mushrooms after rain, developing even more than during the European War. At that time, the popular Great Britain brand cigarettes (produced by the British American Tobacco Company) temporarily disappeared, which can be imagined. However, after the 17th year of the Republic of China, due to the government's increase in taxes and the dumping of foreign goods, Chinese tobacco factories showed a decline. In recent years, they have become even more depressed (see Section 3 of this article for details). Now, the statistics on the number of Chinese tobacco factories in Shanghai (those that set up factories for self-manufacturing) over the years are as follows: Year 5 of the Republic of China: 7; Year 19 of the Republic of China: 9; Year 14 and 15 of the Republic of China: 51; Year 15 of the Republic of China: 105; Year 16 of the Republic of China: 182; Year 17 of the Republic of China: 94; Year 20 of the Republic of China: 64; Year 23 of the Republic of China: 46.

(Note: The numbers are based on the "Report on the Tobacco Industry and the China Bank's Business in the 23rd Year of the Republic of China" compiled by the Shanghai Bank's Research Department. Those who specialize in making cigars are not included.)

Shanghai is the center of industry and commerce in the country. Therefore, the rise and fall of the cigarette industry in Shanghai is sufficient to represent the prosperity and decline of the cigarette industry in the country. (To be continued)

YMCA Amateur Boxing Match Li Menghua Zhou Defeated Buting Shi

Wang Runlan's Striking Technique Was Very Good, Unfortunately, He Was Judged to Have Failed The 32nd Army's Four Athletes Gave Amazing Performances Yesterday

The 32nd Army boxing athletes met with famous Western boxing experts in the city at the YMCA gym at 9:15 last night. Boxing is still in its infancy in our country. The 32nd Army was the earliest to promote it, but it has only been around for two years. Therefore, the outcome of this competition cannot be regarded as a definitive evaluation. Attending the World Games Race Walking Requests to Increase the Number of People Shi Youhui Sends a Letter to the National Sports Association

Our country is preparing to participate in the 11th World Games and has decided on several items, including football, basketball, track and field, swimming, weightlifting, traditional Chinese martial arts, and race walking. However, only one person is assigned to race walking. In order to request an increase in the number of people and for the future of race walking, Shi Youhui of the China Race Walking Association has sent a letter to Shen Siliang of the National Sports Association, which will be forwarded to the selection committee. The letter is excerpted as follows: Respected Sir, it was reported a few days ago that the number of people our country sent to participate in the World Games has been determined: 22 for football, 2 officials; 14 for basketball, 1 official; 12 for track and field, 1 official; 4 for swimming; 4 for weightlifting, 1 official; 6 for traditional Chinese martial arts, 1 official; 1 for race walking, etc. Reading this, I am very surprised. Everyone is ignorant of the art of race walking, and even sportspeople know very little about it. Therefore, the Chinese people do not pay attention to it and regard it with indifference. They do not know that it is only race walking that has added glory to our country in the history of international sports in this city. It has won the championship for six consecutive times, creating a new record for the future. And you, sir, have been enthusiastically promoting race walking, sparing no effort. Three years ago, you instructed us to prepare actively so as to achieve results. This time, at the National Games, it was included in the performance, and the results were close to the world record. Therefore, race walking is more promising for the World Games, which is beyond doubt. Now that 12 people have been set for track and field, 4 for swimming, and 4 for weightlifting, it is inappropriate and unexpected to only send one person for race walking, which is deeply regrettable. Moreover, race walking is a long-distance sport, and race walkers rely heavily on the encourager to encourage them to move forward and strive hard, but they have been omitted, which shows the lack of experience in race walking. For the sake of the future of race walking, I cannot bear to stand idly by. Therefore, I have specially presented my humble opinion: the number of race walkers should also be set at four, so as to become a strong team. I beg you to consider this carefully and forward it to the selection committee, and I hope to receive a reply. I am very grateful. Sincerely, Mr. Shen Siliang of the National Sports Association, Shi Youhui of the China Race Walking Association, February 3rd.

Record of the China Youth Basketball Game Yesterday

The 7th China Youth Basketball League held its 6th week of games yesterday at the China Youth Basketball Hall. A total of five games were played. The first game was between China-France and Nanyang in the school group. The strength of both sides was balanced, and the game was very exciting. In the first half, China-France cooperated with the whole army and won by one goal, slightly frustrating Nanyang. In the second half, Nanyang counterattacked fiercely and won one point over China-France with 16 to 15 despite being in a slump. However, compared with the points lost in the first half, they still lost one point. As a result, China-France won 30 to 29. The second game was between China Youth and Jicui Pavilion in the business group. China Youth has strong players such as Chen Xianglong, Yu Yuzi, and Ou Xianzhu, and its strength is strong, so victory is expected. In the first half, China Youth showed its skills and won Jicui Pavilion 46 to 0 in one go. In the second half, China Youth transferred a large number of troops, but it was still a one-sided game, and it scored 62 to 14. In total, China Youth defeated Jicui Pavilion 106 to 14.

Educational News

Public Concession, Last Year's Education Overview

Private School Subsidies Total Over 370,000 Yuan, Chinese Teachers Hired for Chinese Children's Schools

The report for 1935 by the Director of the Education Department of the Public Concession's工局(Administration), has been submitted to the Board of Directors. It details the educational facilities for Chinese in the Public Concession, the conditions of schools for Western and Japanese children, the progress of bureau-run schools, and the distribution of subsidies for non-bureau-run schools. We have selected the main points for disclosure as follows: As of now, five bureau-run Chinese children's primary schools have been established, with a total of 3,320 students. There is also a well-equipped Western-style building used as a middle school for Chinese girls. In terms of Western schools, two girls' schools have been merged into one, occupying a new, spacious site, and a suitable building has been constructed in the Western District for a Western children's primary school.

Private School Subsidy Amounts: Regarding the subsidies for private schools, in 1931, only five Western-run schools received subsidies from the工部局(Administration). In 1932, Chinese people began to negotiate, and subsidies were issued to Chinese private schools. In 1935, the total amount of subsidies issued was 377,760 yuan, including 208,760 yuan for private Chinese schools and 169,000 yuan for private Western schools. However, this amount was limited, while the number of qualified private schools in the concession was extremely high. There was not enough to go around, which was the greatest difficulty faced by the Special Review Committee for Private School Subsidies this year. Furthermore, Japanese schools requested increased subsidies from the工部局(Administration) due to financial difficulties. The工部局(Administration) allocated an additional special subsidy of 10,000 yuan. Therefore, the number of Japanese schools was given a total of 108,000 yuan in subsidies. Including the above Japanese schools, the Public Concession's 13 private Western schools had a total of 9,292 students. Last year, they received a total of 199,000 yuan in subsidies, an increase of about one-tenth compared to the previous year. The number of Chinese private schools applying for subsidies increased significantly compared to the previous year. This year, 189 schools were verified as qualified, an increase of 44 compared to 1934. The total amount of subsidies received this year was 208,760 yuan, also an increase of slightly one-tenth compared to the previous year. Of this amount, 6,000 yuan was used to improve the school buildings of certain schools. Among all the schools, there were 32 middle schools and 157 primary schools, with a total of 37,808 students. The number of subsidies received by Chinese and Western private schools in recent years is listed below:

Chinese Schools: 1931, None; 1932, 113,986 yuan; 1933, 138,811 yuan; 1934, 186,375 yuan; 1935, 208,760 yuan.

Western Schools: 1931, 107,692 yuan; 1932, Same as before; 1933, 141,608 yuan; 1934, 153,850 yuan; 1935, 169,000 yuan.

1935 Annual Report further states: Due to financial difficulties this year, the original educational construction plan had to be continuously postponed. However, the Board of Directors has resolved that when the financial situation improves slightly in the future, the original plan will be carefully reconsidered. Regarding Chinese educational facilities, at the end of last year, the Board of Directors resolved to add a Chinese children's primary school at the old site of the Western Boys' School on Wenzaishi Road. If no other incidents occur in 1936, the expenses for the establishment of this school will be included in the budget.

Overview of Bureau-Run Chinese Children's Schools: The工部局(Administration) Girls' Middle School is located at No. 9 Singapore Road. The school building is newly built, with 500 students receiving the most modern education and training. Currently, there are a total of 10 bureau-run Chinese children's schools (day schools) and 1 night school, with a total of 6,383 students, an increase of 2,860 students compared to 1931, accounting for 81%.

In 1934, the工部局(Administration) Education Department established a subcommittee to investigate the five bureau-run Chinese middle schools and hold a joint examination to eliminate inconsistencies in standards upon graduation. After approval, the following resolutions were submitted to the Board of Directors for approval:

In June 1935, the five bureau-run Chinese middle schools will hold a joint examination at a central location. The questions should be consistent with the existing curriculum of each school, with room for selection and exchange to suit the scope of each school's curriculum.

The examination of certain subjects by outsiders will be postponed until the courses in each school are standardized and the number of participants in the Education Bureau's middle school examination is determined, then further discussion will be held.

Students of bureau-run middle schools should be encouraged to participate in the Education Bureau's middle school examination.

The above resolutions were made because the courses in each school are not yet completely the same, and it is not appropriate to rush to standardize them. Regarding the participation of students from bureau-run middle schools in the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau's examination, it is because the various middle schools established by the 工部局(Administration) have been specially recognized by the Ministry of Education of the National Government, so students can participate in the examinations held by the Chinese authorities themselves.

Subsequently, the first joint examination of the five bureau-run middle schools was held in early June at Gezhi Public School. An examination committee was organized, with the principals of the five schools as the core, supplemented by an equal number of examiners from each school. 55 senior high school students participated in the examination. 40 students who passed the examination were awarded graduation certificates, of which 15 students with excellent results and an average score of over 80 were classified as excellent. This is a general overview of the 1935 joint examination of bureau-run middle schools.

Gradual Reduction of Western Teachers: According to the original policy of the工部局(Administration), Chinese teachers should be hired as much as possible in the bureau-run Chinese schools to replace Western teachers. Therefore, in the early spring of 1935, the 工部局(Administration) Education Department conducted a detailed discussion on whether the Western teachers in each school could be further reduced. After consideration, it was decided to first hire several Chinese teachers to teach subjects such as science and mathematics, and then hire Chinese teachers to teach English in the future.

Related to this matter, the reports of each school generally stated that students' Chinese studies have made significant progress. For example, students at Yucai Public School have made significant progress in Chinese composition, with considerable ideas and styles. Other subjects such as civics and geography have also achieved excellent results. The school library has also added a large number of Chinese books, which is of great benefit to the students' moral character. Furthermore, the report from Gezhi Public School also stated that two Western teachers had resigned from the school last year, so Chinese teachers have been used to teach English to junior students. However, a few Western English teachers are still retained in each grade to avoid overly rapid changes. Geography has been changed to Chinese textbooks, and other science and mathematics subjects are also gradually being taught in Chinese, starting with the junior grades. Furthermore, the school authorities reward students with outstanding Chinese composition in each grade to encourage students to study Chinese. This also shows the importance that the bureau-run schools attach to Chinese.

Increasing Development of Ball Sports: The annual reports of the Chinese children's schools established by the 工部局(Administration) are generally divided into two types: middle schools and primary schools. Generally speaking about the middle schools (including one girls' middle school), students' work is generally required to be quiet and diligent. However, students' interest in physical education and various sports is increasing. For example, the number of students participating in various sports at Yucai Public School has suddenly increased dramatically. The school's previous records have been broken in as many as four events. The football, basketball, and volleyball teams of Nie Zhongcheng Public School have achieved remarkable results. In addition to focusing on physical education, students at the Girls' Middle School also attach great importance to social life, including organizations such as drama clubs, debate clubs, and dance clubs.

In terms of primary schools, the total number of students in the spring and autumn of 1935 was 3,169 and 3,249 respectively. The attendance rate was 92%. The number of applicants at each school generally far exceeded the quota, especially at the Xinzha Road Western District Primary School. The courses at each school are generally conducted in accordance with the regulations of the Ministry of Education.

The entrance examinations for each middle school were held in mid-June. A total of 124 students participated in the examination, of which 46 were graduates of bureau-run primary schools. Based on the examination results, scholarships were awarded to six graduates from bureau-run and non-bureau-run primary schools. A total of 269 students graduated this year. Before graduation, the Shanghai United Industries Guidance Society provided sufficient assistance to each student's future. Students from poor families and with excellent academic performance were given financial assistance. The funds were donated voluntarily by each school. In addition, the bureau-run schools have had an alumni association since 1933, and each school has established its own branch.

Furthermore, the number of students at the Jingzhou Road Night School this year was 306 in the spring and 455 in the autumn. These students are all students who work during the day. At the end of the spring semester, an examination was held, and diplomas were awarded to seven students. Their level is equivalent to that of graduates from other primary schools. They have all studied at the night school for a full year.

Public Concession Student Statistics: According to statistics on the total number of Chinese and foreign students in the Shanghai Public Concession, excluding non-bureau-run and middle and primary schools unrelated to the 工部局(Administration), the total number of students in various middle and primary schools owned by the bureau or subsidized by the bureau is 51,041, including 2,694 students in bureau-run Chinese middle schools, 3,689 students in bureau-run Chinese primary schools, 4,555 students in subsidized Chinese middle schools, 33,253 students in subsidized Chinese primary schools, 1,598 students in bureau-run Western schools, and 5,252 students in subsidized Western schools.

Furthermore, an analysis of the nationalities of students in the bureau-run Western schools shows that the 1,598 students come from 37 nationalities, with British accounting for the most, at 46%. The remaining nationalities are Russian at 18%, American at 8%, Portuguese at 5%, Japanese at 3%, and the remaining 20% being children from other countries.

Liu Haisu and Others Initiate the Organization of the China Fine Arts Association

The first preparatory meeting was held yesterday, and the association is scheduled to be established on March 15th.

In order to develop the fine arts and create the art of the times, more than 140 people from the art world, including Liu Haisu, jointly initiated the organization of the China Fine Arts Association as a central organization. They have convened a meeting of the initiators and the first preparatory meeting, and plan to hold the inaugural meeting on March 15th. They are now actively soliciting members. The details are as follows:

Meeting of Initiators: The association held a meeting of initiators the other day at No. 504 Lafayette Road. Those present included Liu Haisu, Wang Jiyuan, Ma Gongyu, Ni Yide, Xu Xuangu, He Mingqi, Yan Kechang, Xie Haiyan, Zhang Chengjiang, Pan Yuliang, Xie Gongzhan, Xiang Peiliang, Liu Kang, Chen Renhao, Wang Yuanbo, Li Jian, and others, totaling more than 20 people. Liu Haisu was the chairman, and Xie Haiyan was the secretary.

Organizational Aim: First, Chairman Liu Haisu reported on the aim of initiating the organization of the China Fine Arts Association, stating that China is an ancient country with the most brilliant culture, and the great achievements of fine arts in various dynasties surpass those of all countries in the world. But what has been presented to us in recent years? Those who talk about the history of modern culture do not even put us in their eyes. In other words, we have no modern culture. Those of us who are born in modern China and are involved in the fine arts and culture world feel ashamed to death when we think about it. In the past, I and others, considering that the prosperity and strength of a country and nation are not entirely based on strong ships and powerful artillery, but that its international status is determined by the rise and fall of culture, and that fine arts are a major field of culture, wanted to do their part for the society and nation in this major field. Therefore, the establishment of fine arts schools was initiated to cultivate basic people, and then the Tianma Association was initiated to carry out a general art movement. The greatness of its achievements and the depth of its impact can be said to have completed its initial journey in the early modern art world. Later, because I left the country in a hurry, the Tianma Association also ceased to exist in name. After returning from two trips to Europe, I saw that the art world was even more decadent and desolate than in the past. I repeatedly thought about how to revitalize it. On January 6th, I and the initiators present held the first discussion meeting at Hailu on Lafayette Road and initiated the organization of this association to unite comrades in the fine arts world and work together to develop the fine arts, taking this association as the central organization to create an art of the times and complete our historical mission, washing away the shame of having no modern culture.

Key Resolutions: Following the discussion, the following resolutions were made: The association should handle the application for permission. It was resolved that the application should be signed by the initiators according to the legal number of people. When applying for permission according to the Law on the Organization of People's Groups, representatives of the initiators should be elected to be responsible for external affairs. It was resolved to elect Liu Haisu as the representative of the initiators. Preparatory personnel should be elected to be responsible for carrying out the preparations. It was resolved to elect Liu Haisu, Wang Jiyuan, Ma Gongyu, Ni Yide, Xie Haiyan, Yan Kechang, Xie Gongzhan, and Xiang Peiliang as the preparatory members, with Liu Haisu as the convener. The draft articles of association were discussed, and it was resolved that the draft articles of association should be adopted in principle, and Xie Haiyan, Xiang Peiliang, Yan Kechang, and Ni Yide should revise them. How to carry out the collection of members was discussed and it was resolved: Members should be collected separately by the initiators. Members should be collected by mail. How to plan the preparatory funds for the association was discussed, and it was resolved that the funds should be freely donated by the initiators. The date of the inaugural meeting of the association was decided to be March 15th. The address of the association was decided to be temporarily at No. 440 Caishi Road. How the association emblem should be designed was discussed, and it was resolved: Liu Haisu, Wang Jiyuan, Ma Gongyu, Yan Kechang, Xiang Peiliang, Ni Yide, Xie Haiyan, He Mingzhai, Li Jian, Wang Baiyuan, Zheng Yuebo, Fang Bingchao, Zhou Duo, Bi Zheng, Liu Kang, and Chen Renhao were elected to design and draw the emblem.

First Preparatory Meeting: The association held its first preparatory meeting yesterday. Those present included Liu Haisu, Wang Jiyuan, Ma Gongyu, Ni Yide, Xie Haiyan, Yan Kechang, Xie Gongzhan, and Xiang Peiliang. Liu Haisu was the chairman. Duties were assigned, and Liu Haisu, Wang Jiyuan, and Ma Gongyu were appointed as executive directors, Yan Kechang as the organizer, Xie Haiyan and Ni Yide as the secretaries, Zhang Chengjiang as the accountant, and Xie Gongzhan as the public relations officer. The inaugural meeting will be held on March 15th at the Chinese Arts and Crafts Society. Members are now being actively solicited. It is reported that Jing Hengyi, Mei Lanfang, Chen Shuren, and others will join.

Children's Educational Novel: Little Men (I) (VI) (VII)

— Original by Louisa M. Alcott, translated by Zheng Xiaocang

This confession was not well written, the handwriting was also hasty, leaving many ink spots, and it was very short; but Don regarded it as a treasure; after Mr. Bhaer read it, Don ran to his side, his eyes clear, his attitude simple and respectful—this is what they had always taught him to be—but he said with a slightly trembling voice:

"I said I shouldn't lie, please forgive me, sir."

"This is a well-intentioned lie, Don, I cannot but forgive this, but you see it is useless," Mr. Bhaer said, putting one hand on each shoulder, his face full of love and comfort.

"This keeps the boys from bothering Nat anymore. That's what I did it for. He can't take the pain, I don't mind," Don said, as if after a long, painful silence, he frankly told his innermost thoughts.

"How could you do that? You treat me so well," Nat said, trembling, wishing he could hug his friend and cry; both of these were childish behaviors, and if he had really done it, Don would have learned to be ashamed and have nowhere to hide.

"Now everything is fine, old friend, so don't be a fool anymore," he said, swallowing a large lump of resentment in his throat, and laughing heartily, which he hadn't done for weeks. He then asked eagerly, "I wonder if Mrs. Bhaer knows?"

Page 17

Spring and Autumn

Paintings of Abyssinia

— (Ning Yu)

I once saw paintings from Abyssinia somewhere. The subjects were mostly about war and religion: the 1896 Battle of Adwa between the Abyssinians and the Italians, the Garden of Eden, the war between good and evil, etc. One of their most striking features was that good people were always painted frontally, while bad people were only painted in profile. For example, the Italians who waged war against Abyssinia were all painted in profile, while their own soldiers were all painted frontally, even though their muskets were aimed directly at the enemy.

This lack of perspective, this peculiar technique, seems very naive from an artistic point of view. However, they aroused my inexplicable fondness.

China has a similar expression, which is the application of facial makeup in drama. Using different colors and strokes to distinguish clearly between good and evil people is a little more technically advanced. But many viewers do not understand the distinction, and it is not as clear as the Abyssinian paintings.

So I thought: if the people in the world were truly divided into good and evil, and expressed using the Abyssinian method, wouldn't it be much easier to be a person than it is now? At the very least, it would be worth calling out a few times when people look at it! I just think that good people should be painted in profile and bad people should be painted frontally, because now it is a world where bad people are in front.

Carved Dwarf Drum

— Chen Yuling

Dwarf Drum, a man from Minhou, whose name is lost, was short in stature with a large belly, so he was called Dwarf Drum. The mountains of Min produce a lot of wood, the roots of which are intertwined and gnarled, and are known for their sturdiness. Woodworkers carve them into figures, flowers, and the like, but Dwarf Drum's skill is particularly refined. However, Dwarf Drum had a strange habit: every time he received wages, he would spend them all before starting work. If he had leftover grain in his jar, he would always abandon his work to play. He traveled among nobles and high officials, never flattering them to gain favor. Chen Zichang, the son of Minister Chen of Luojiang, and a predecessor of Grand Tutor Tao'an, summoned Dwarf Drum to carve wood. The Chen family was at the height of its power, accustomed to issuing commands, and did not treat Dwarf Drum with respect. Dwarf Drum was displeased. He responded vaguely, and the work was delayed for a long time without completion. When servants were sent to check on him, the basic form was still not there. Enraged, Chen imprisoned him. Dwarf Drum, feeling unhappy in prison, used his work to pass the time, creating several figures, which he returned to the minister, and was released. The former prefect Liu Buxi treated Dwarf Drum with exceptional kindness, providing him with food and drink whenever he came, along with other delicacies he liked. Dwarf Drum, after eating and drinking to his fill, would leave immediately, returning another day. After Dwarf Drum had troubled his master several times, he also wanted to do something for him, so he asked the master, "Do you have fine wood you would like me to carve?" The Liu family had a rich store of wood, and selected the best pieces to give to Dwarf Drum, without setting a deadline. Dwarf Drum was sure to repay the favor and put extra effort into it. Dwarf Drum had a disciple named Mou, whose carving of figures was also quite admirable. Dwarf Drum said, "You are only good at grinding and polishing, not worth mentioning in terms of knife skills. A knife is only valuable if it boosts its owner, but yours are all dull and flat." The disciple said, "Please tell me the way to sharpen and uplift them." Dwarf Drum said, "This cannot be explained in words." Could Dwarf Drum be keeping something secret, or is skill really something that cannot be taught? Someone in the market showed him a printed image of a sacred statue carved by Duanmu in boxwood. Dwarf Drum said, "Everywhere is simple and rustic, everywhere is spiritual. People today know the spiritual is spiritual, but they don't know the rustic is spiritual." Tasting his words, one realizes he understands calligraphy and painting, but I have never seen him hold a brush to do them. Dwarf Drum was famous between the Guangxu and Xuantong eras, and died around the beginning of the Republic of China. He had a solitary nature, so he didn't produce much. What I have seen includes a Bodhidharma, less than a foot tall, with extremely lively posture. The wood had a flaw on the back, protruding out and impossible to carve, so he took advantage of the shape to make him carry a bamboo hat. Another is a Drunken Immortal, lying on his back with his head uncovered, his hair a tangled mess of who knows how many thousands of strands. One leg is bent, one stretched out, with all the muscles and bones exposed, and the straw sandals he wears are also exquisitely made. These two were seen at the home of Liu Zhongzan, my father's colleague, who was a cousin of Buxi.

A Record of Silhouette Artist Huang Yinian

— Wang Shouqiu

A few months ago, a silhouette artist came to Nanjing, who could cut a profile portrait from a piece of paper in just three or four minutes. It could be said to be an extraordinary skill, as it could be cut so vividly!

This silhouette artist's surname is Huang, his name is Yinian. He is a graduate of the Xinhua Fine Arts School in Shanghai. He had filmed the movie "Guangming" in the film section of the Nanchang Headquarters. He has considerable research on woodcuts and carvings. Later, he came up with this silhouette method from woodcuts and carvings. He has received a lot of praise. So he came to Nanjing and set up the sign of silhouette artist. Because this kind of silhouette was rare in the past, many people in the capital went to have their silhouettes cut. His price for silhouette is one yuan per person. He also set up a preferential treatment for students. All students who come to cut will be charged half price, only five corners will do. According to Mr. Huang, this kind of silhouette is not a valuable thing. However, it requires research on carving and woodcut. Because it is not difficult to cut a silhouette of a person, but it is not easy to cut it vividly and accurately!

I have always said: Chinese art is really worthy of admiration. Take the woman who cuts patterns, for example. They can cut various ingenious patterns casually. If you do not have artistic talent, it seems that you cannot cut it so satisfactorily. It is already not easy to cut patterns, and it is certainly more difficult to cut a person's silhouette! So I said that your silhouette is half research and half talent.

The Story of the Viola (Alto Violin)

— Yue Qi

I am one who is not often noticed. My name is Viola. I can't catch up with my petite and young sister, the Violin, who is so splendid, nor as large and loud as my brother, "Cello"—the Bass Viola.

Because of my close relationship with famous figures in "strings", my personality has lost a lot. I am always helping others, mixing with their tones, and not paying much attention to myself.

At first, I also set off the treble; after many years, the Violin replaced my position. Now, I specialize in alto or sub-alto. My style is similar to the Violin, but my body is one-fifth larger than hers. My sound is one-fifth lower than the Violin, my strings are slightly thicker, and my bow is slightly shorter and thicker. However, whether plucked with fingers or pulled by hand, I can make the same tones as my versatile sister. Those who criticize me say that I am sad, indifferent, and clumsy; but I am confident that my treble is very soft and beautiful.

The famous composer, in his symphony "Harold in Italy," regarded me as an important character. Wagner repeatedly invited me to play a role. In orchestras that can recognize my expressive genius, my position is gradually becoming more important.

I hope I will always be willing to play a role in accompaniment music, and occupy a position with other instruments in the second and third part music. I am called "the philosopher of stringed instruments" because I have a humble nature that is willing to help others.

Many beginners who can't play the Violin well give me a successful second chance, because they should learn from me before learning the Violin.

A Casual Talk on Cursive Script

— Zhen Lü

The strength of cursive script lies in the whole piece, just like the completion of an article. It is not flawed by one or two characters; its difficulty also lies in this. What it has most in common with an article, which cannot be ignored, is that it moves with energy; although there are many twists and turns in the middle, the whole must seek consistency, which is called a good work. If, when writing, emotions arise and the momentum changes, wonderful interests will naturally be achieved, which cannot be predetermined. Predetermination leads to nothing, which is the constant principle of all artistic endeavors. Don't you see that when writing cursive script in a drunken state, it often becomes more and more spirited? How can I know myself?

In our country's calligraphy, regular, cursive, clerical, and seal scripts each reach their own wonders, but cursive script takes the strengths of each style and integrates them into a great achievement, and intricately transforms them, thus purely proceeding with artistic conditions and being rich in the beauty of curves. Therefore, cursive script is in harmony with all calligraphy, and it is especially suitable for freehand sketching calligraphy. If you use the method of cursive script to paint, it must be a vivid painting; if you can use the method of painting to write cursive script, that is called cursive script. There are those in the world who spend their whole lives painting without knowing what cursive script is, but there is no one who can recognize the wonders of cursive script without knowing painting, and there is no one who is good at cursive script but does not understand the principles of painting. This is because painting has the interest of cursive script, while cursive script fully possesses the many strengths of painting.

Cannot Run Fast

—

Some say that those who excel in cursive script may not also be good at regular script, or even that it is unnecessary. This is a fallacy, not something that someone who understands would say. Cursive script is transformed from running script, and running script comes from regular script; this is the fixed step in our country's calligraphy, and the principle can also be measured. If we use the position of cursive script as myself, then running script is my father and regular script is my grandfather. Who says I can do cursive but not regular? Isn't that a reckless person who forgets his ancestors? The ancients said, "Regular script is like standing, running script is like walking, cursive script is like running," which is indeed a close analogy. It is rare in the world to find someone who can only run but cannot stand. However, regular script is like standing, emphasizing stillness, while cursive script is like running, emphasizing movement. Liking movement and disliking stillness is the constant feeling of ordinary people. Therefore, there are those who enjoy writing cursive script, falsely claiming that they cannot do regular script, avoiding what they do not want to do. People then follow suit and make excuses for them. If someone comes along who becomes famous for cursive script but cannot do regular script, then their cursive script is like a wild fox spirit, and there will be little good in the end. They will only be stealing names and deceiving the world! Therefore, "a gentleman devotes himself to the root." Those who aspire to cursive script cannot fail to think of this.

The world is so big, and there are many kinds of people. They are distinguished by color, and the weak are bullied by the strong. They are accustomed to being far apart, but in the beginning, they were the same. "Mama" and "Papa" come from childhood; the beginning of language is no different between Chinese and foreigners. Looking into the writing, the evolution needs a period, tying knots to record events, and the line is maintained. Crab-like winding is mature in the West; our country uses pictographs, bird tracks and beast hooves. People have the same heart, and hearts have the same reason. Tracing its origin, it is probably so! The text changes gradually, and it becomes what we see today. Our Chinese set of books is the fixed image of painting shapes; archaeologists should have the same view. Then the unique beauty and reason of our calligraphy, but Qinxi has no name here, because it is difficult to seek its deep understanding because of the different paths it takes. The matter is true, and it is clearly visible! Therefore, the book has the inscriptions on bells and tripods, and stone drums, which is the pattern school of painting. The book has passed through the official script through the Han and Wei Dynasties, and it has entered the regular script. The painting has the Cubist school and the Impressionist school. Each has its own appearance, which takes a lot of people's exploration to find a similar one. If the book becomes cursive, it will increase its complexity, twists and turns, and windings. It will expand its use of pen and ink, and it will not be the realm of painting into sketching? Since my book has the bone and tire of painting, and the cursive script is added to make it clearer, we will see that our people will eventually have a picture-like script to show the world, so as to invite the mind of those who are knowledgeable!

Ink Marks on Bamboo Leaves

— (Huangshan Nong)

Yixian County is surrounded by mountains and has excellent scenery. About five miles away from Taoyuan Cave, there are many bamboos, thick and dense. The leaves of ordinary bamboo are green, but the ones produced here are black, as if dyed with ink. Even after a long period of rain and sun, the color does not fade, which is very peculiar. Asking the locals, there are two explanations: one is that Li Qinglian of the Tang Dynasty once traveled here and wrote poems on the stone wall, splashing the remaining ink on the bamboo, like the story of Xiangfei's mottled bamboo. Another explanation is that the nearby coal mines are rich, and they are usually affected by its quality, resulting in this difference. The former is a myth, which cannot be investigated. Although the latter has a little reason, there are many bamboo-producing areas in the coal area, but those whose leaves are black have never been heard before, which is also a question.

Little Western Paradise

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Twenty-Three: The Resolute Filing of a Lawsuit After Eloquent Talk Around the Room, and the Forgetting of Past Grievances for Profit After Pouring Wine in Nostalgic Friendship

Wang Shicheng smiled and said, "We are selling property. As long as someone gives us the price, we can sell it. We don't necessarily recognize anyone." Jia Duocai cupped his hands and said, "That's good. The location and time are written on my note. Let's talk face-to-face tomorrow morning." Wang Shicheng said, "However, since we are changing buyers, I can't make the decision alone. I have to ask a gentleman from my clan to come out and be jointly responsible." Jia Duocai said, "Then please ask that gentleman to come with you. Although I don't know him, we will get acquainted when we meet, and we will be friends the second time we meet. Please tell your esteemed kinsman that I welcome him to talk." Wang Shicheng said, "Since Mr. Zi has such good intentions, I will definitely bring him along." Jia Duocai heard him use the last character of his name as his surname, and wanted to correct him, but Wang Shicheng hurriedly walked away, and it was too late to correct him. He planned in his heart that if this deal succeeds, he can at least get three thousand yuan from the large amount of money. With the land, he can also get the construction company's project in his hands, and he can make a fortune on this. It's really that when wealth comes, even the door can't stop it. He had long wanted to find a piece of land next to the future railway station, but no matter what he did, he couldn't buy one piece of land. Unexpectedly, it happened by chance, and such a large piece of land was for sale, and with just a few words, he got the matter into his hands. He was so happy that he immediately threw the matter of Yueying to the back of his mind, and lay down on the bed freely and comfortably. Although he was a person who liked to sleep late, when he arrived in Xi'an, he had to follow the locals and get up early. The locals get up at five o'clock, and Jia Duocai has no choice but to get up at seven or eight o'clock. Every morning, he stays at home, drinking tea and eating snacks, and only goes out after ten o'clock, but today is different. He got up at five o'clock, just like the people of Xi'an. Seeing that the door of Mr. Jin's room next door was tightly closed, he hurriedly washed his face, drank a cup of tea, and went out without waiting for the local newspaper to be delivered. He couldn't help but smile in his heart. Jin Ziqiang is still in his dream, and the deal that he has put so much effort into has been unknowingly snatched by me. After he gets up and can't see me, he won't be on guard. (Three Hundred and Ninety-Nine)

Preface to Ma Gongyu's Seal Album

— Posthumous Work of Sun Deqian

Mr. Ma Gongyu of Yongjia is a gentleman of erudition today. He inherited his family learning at a young age and was skilled in poetry and prose. He was good at painting and calligraphy, and especially proficient in seal carving. He brought out his seal album and asked for an inscription. I have never studied the words of epigraphy. How can I be like Yuan Yan, who has high reputation, and can be compared to Chen Si? How can I dare to comment rashly? However, I have heard that the principle of writing and calligraphy is the same. Chasing and carving for pleasure, did Xiqi not chant elegantly? Exhausting the momentum of the tiger warrior, the skill is ingenious and divine. Gongyu's wonderful creation is natural, and the branch advances to the Tao. It is appropriate that they are linked together like pearls and compete for brilliance, and that the secret treasures are cherished together. The seal is used for trust. The characters follow the festival. The symbol is auspicious, and Zhou is honored. Its use is parallel to the seal, and the distinction between high and low is strict in Qin. The red sign touches the spirit, the yellow spirit harmonizes virtue, the five numbers seek契, and the additions make a speech. Hundred officials govern, and make different systems by distinguishing. As for the breaking of jade since Wei, it is said to be the private affairs of Cao Huan. Yuan Yi began to cast copper from the system of Wang Mian. This is the source that can be reached, and its function is to publicize the letter. The body of the seal is modeled. Qin has a special book. The seal is called "Miu Zhuan", and it comes from a long way. Since the recent world, the authors have been crowded. Only Zhejiang and Wan, the flow and distinction flourished. Exploring the origin of Huang Jie and following the old man of Chen Si, establish a special door and each practice, pass the bowl to each other, and remove the strange changes of the township wall, hold the bucket without concealing, and the gods and rules, is it not beautiful? Only if there is no new change, can evil replace the male? Therefore, Qi and Lu are facing the mud, and the world is gradually widespread. This is the creation of the pot house, and the runners respond to it. It is like another rain competing for newness, and the Yuan wind alone fans it. Gongyu is naturally precise and accumulated. The understanding of the cow is so rich. The art of decomposing the ox is like a new grinding. According to the formula of collecting foxes, he can repair the old text. If Yuan Ting's Liu Fen, should know the strange characters. Then he is familiar with stone carvings, and the Huju foot is a famous family. Although the flower is beautiful, he has been good at elegance since childhood. Depending on the grass, he is charming, and he is different and lucky. Shangu saw the withdrawal of the hermit, and the Qiu壑 passed the spirit of Zijing. Those who spread the world far away are not all here. However, this Hongzhao will stay for a long time, and the rhinoceros heart will operate independently. Looking at the hundreds of names above Kan, I laugh alone in a volume. It has made it difficult to speak of the sea, and to hide the mountains as prosperous. I am ashamed to write, and I am tired of carving the dragon. The white snow is high, and I know that the eyes of the harmony are few. Qingyun Kufu, fortunately, the benefits of 相得 are more obvious.
