Miscellaneous Thoughts

— Whistle

The other day, Mr. Suma Yakichiro, First Class Secretary of the Japanese Embassy and concurrently Consul-General stationed in Beijing, returned to Shanghai on orders, intending to go to Beijing to meet with Foreign Minister Zhang and present his views on Sino-Japanese relations. When Suma passed through Shanghai, he told Japanese reporters that during his return to Japan, he had consulted with Foreign Minister Hirota, military authorities, and important figures from both the government and the public. They had a new understanding of the Sino-Japanese problem, and some were worried about the future of Sino-Japanese relations, even questioning the need for Sino-Japanese conferences.

As the saying goes, "The emperor is not anxious, but the eunuch is frantic," and "The sheep is not anxious, but the tiger is frantic." It's truly a laughing matter. Japan is the country engaging in aggression, and our country is the one being invaded. Our people should be worried but are not, while the Japanese should not be worried but are. This is worrying about what others don't usually worry about and not worrying about what others should worry about. I advise the Japanese to put their minds at ease and do whatever they want without concern.

The other day, a certain newspaper reported that Prince De had declared the establishment of an "Autonomous Government" in Chahar Province, with the government located in Zhangbei, claiming to be a continuation of the Yuan Dynasty. The flag of the autonomous government is red, yellow, blue, and white. Recently, Prince De took a plane given by the Japanese some time ago to Xinjing in Manchuria for several discussions. It is said that an agreement was reached with Puyi, with Manchuria supplying military supplies to the new Mongolian government, and so on.

Later, we received a telegram from the Central News Agency correcting this matter, stating that Prince De had sent a telegram to clarify the situation. I generally do not trust foreign newspapers and news agencies because they specialize in spreading rumors. Therefore, when I read ancient books, I am reminded of the saying, "To believe everything written in a book is worse than having no book at all," and I cannot help but feel emotional.

Mr. Hu Hanmin, who has been the focus of Chinese and foreign attention, has already returned to China and will soon go to Beijing to preside over the affairs of the Central Standing Committee. He recently made a statement in Hong Kong, saying, "In short, the Party should be restored to a party with principles and spirit, and strive to eliminate the past mistakes of fragmentation and disunity, in order to continue the Party's unfinished great cause. The government should be transformed into a responsible and capable government, and strive to correct the past mistakes of fear and complacency, in order to shoulder the heavy responsibility of resolving national crises and building the nation."

These few sentences are truly valuable. However, in recent times, important figures have had a common problem: what they say offstage often does not match the reality onstage. In their time out of power, they speak eloquently, but once they are in power, they become silent and cannot implement their proposals from when they were out of power. At this moment, I can only hope that after Mr. Hu Hanmin takes office, he can fulfill everything he has said now.

The newly appointed Japanese Ambassador to China, Mr. Ariyoshi Akira, recently made a statement to the press, saying that Chinese diplomacy has always adopted the policy of "using barbarians to control barbarians" and "befriending distant states and attacking nearby ones." Therefore, Japan should automatically make the European and American countries understand Japan's position on China, and adopt a policy of exerting its strength, being outwardly calm and inwardly anxious.

The so-called policy of being outwardly calm and inwardly anxious is Foreign Minister Hirota's "duck diplomacy"—appearing calm on the surface while secretly and rapidly advancing. Their policy has always been consistent: striving to attack. But what is our government's policy? What good policies do we have to deal with this? We really do not know. However, one thing is certain: do not be deceived by the Japanese. They are working secretly, and we should work openly. We would rather suffer a clear loss than a hidden one.

Firecrackers

— Toya Tono

The south end of Dingjia Street is an open space. The withered yellow grass is spread flat on the ground, adorned with scattered firecracker skins, as if there is a hint of spring. A telephone pole stands upright in the open space, greeting the passing wind.

A group of children are chattering noisily on the grass, as if the New Year has set their hearts ablaze.

Little Jiu had just been beaten by his mother and ran out in anger. Seeing the joy of the group, he wiped his snot with his hand and squeezed into the crowd:

— Little Jinzi, come here!

Little Jinzi is about the same age as him: eight or nine years old. No, once the New Year arrives, he will be ten years old. His face is covered in dust, his eyes are wide open, and his eyebrows move mischievously. He turns around, sees Little Jiu, sees Little Jiu's snot, and wipes his hand on his cheek

— Shameless, you're dripping snot!

Little Jiu "hmphs" and sniffs. He asks who is setting off firecrackers here, his eyes still searching through the crowd.

— Come here, I'll tell you, — Little Jiu comes over — Do you have any money to buy firecrackers?

Little Jiu rolls his eyes, shakes his head, and whispers something into Little Jinzi's ear that only the two of them can hear. Little Jinzi laughs, the firecrackers sounding happily, as if deliberately showing off to him. He thinks for a moment and says:

— What if it doesn't work? He definitely won't be willing... he's a dog ×: allowed in but not allowed out!

When the two of them squeeze back into the crowd, their eyes are both fixed on the young master Jin, who is standing in the middle. He is not very tall to begin with, and a bit fat, making him seem even shorter and clumsier. He has small eyes and is holding a shoe box in his hand. The shoe box is full of valuable firecrackers, and he is holding a large handful of incense sticks, none of which are lit. He takes out a string of firecrackers, lights an incense stick, and hands it to his good buddy Fusheng, telling him to set them off while he listens. Fusheng is also clumsy, afraid but unable to avoid lighting the firecrackers, often thinking he has lit them and running away in fright. Young Master Jin takes his hands away from his ears and says with a simple smile:

— You're such a scaredy-cat, you don't dare to set them off!

Little Jinzi sees this as an opportunity, sidles over, and says:

— Hey, between brothers, who cares who sets them off, I'll set them off for you! He pats Fusheng's shoulder as he speaks. Fusheng looks at his face in surprise, and then feels humiliated, ignoring him and lighting his own firecrackers. Who knew one would hit Little Jiu's leg, Little Jiu takes a step forward, comes over, glares, puts his hands on his waist, gives Little Jinzi a wink, and kicks Fusheng with his leg:

— Have these gentlemen offended you? Hit these people!

Fusheng looks at Little Jiu even more timidly, like a sheep, not daring to move, but also unwilling to show weakness, and looks at Young Master Jin. Young Master Jin is waiting foolishly and idiotically, and when he sees him looking at him, he musters his courage and says:

— He's so unreasonable, he's clearly bullying people, you should just listen to him, why are you stirring up trouble?

— That's right, I'm setting off my firecrackers, you listen to yours, why are you looking for trouble...

These people are so good, hiring someone to set off firecrackers without spending money, and even having someone give them firecrackers!

The bystanders also want to watch the fun, some laugh gloatingly, some say sarcastic things, as if everyone is surrounded by spring. Little Jiu sniffs, pinches his nose, and hums:

Who's bullying you? You have to look at the owner when you beat a dog. Who are you? Stop talking nonsense, buddy, give us some to set off...

— Why should I...

Little Jinzi and Little Jiu's fists extend at the same time: Because of this. At the same time, they walk towards Young Master Jin, who looks at the two black, annoying fists, afraid that they will fall on him and dirty his robes, and runs away. But where can he run? There are people all around! He is grabbed by Little Jinzi at once, running around the telephone pole with Little Jinzi chasing him. Little Jiu tangles Fusheng so he can't come over to help. Young Master Jin runs with difficulty, shouting: "Fusheng, go call the family!" His face is red and he wants to sweat. He slips under his feet, not knowing what he has stumbled on, and "thump!" he falls on the grass like a cloth bag, chewing on the grass like a sheep. A large box of red, green, and flowered firecrackers are scattered all over the ground. Little Jinzi ignores Young Master Jin, opens his lapel? And puts them in by handfuls:

— Little Jiu, forget about him, come and pick them up! ...Mother ×, what are you snatching!

He grabs at the same time as the other children while shouting to Little Jiu. There is nothing left on the ground. Looking up, Young Master Jin has not gotten up, lying on the ground, sweat dripping from his face. He goes over and sits on him, saying:

— You wouldn't be a good person. If you had just given them, nothing would have happened. But, I ask you: are you afraid of me? Say! Are you afraid? How many generations are you afraid? ...No! ...At least a hundred generations! Also, what does your mother call who ×, say it, say "Little Jinzi ×"!

The surrounding people laugh and cheer. Little Jiu kneels on the ground with Fusheng's hands tied behind his back, kicks him in the back with one foot, "thwack" and Fusheng falls like a dead body, turning his head around.

Little Jinzi, let's go, let's set off firecrackers!

They had just left the lawn when they heard the Jin family yelling:

— Who is that bastard provoking the young master...

— Mother ×! These people! ...Let's go Little Jiu, let's go set them off!

Little Jinzi puts his arm on Little Jiu's back and walks away intimately.

Assassination Case (Continued from Yesterday)

— Ye Lai

"To hell with this, I really don't want to continue doing it anymore. There's only outgoing expenses and no incoming income. But how are you going to clear the accounts? This news cannot be spread. Once it's spread, all the debts will become a problem. It's very troublesome!"

"There's no savings left now either." Huang Jiaxing said, and thought for a moment: "We only have a little more than ten thousand here. You lost more than thirty thousand in the past. What should we do? We'll divide up all the more than ten thousand in the company, but you have to clear up the more than thirty thousand that you personally lost."

A Jun seemed to have been doused with a bucket of cold water. The words of Jiaxing were tying knots in his heart, going around in circles. After a while, the flames in his heart burned into those gray and tired eyes. He thought for a moment. He felt that if Jiaxing didn't take out the more than fifty thousand in cash in his hands to divide, it would be like being insulted and deceived by Jiaxing. He gritted his teeth and stared angrily at Jiaxing, who was still smiling.

However, Huang Jiaxing didn't seem to feel that A Jun hated him, and had suddenly become an enemy. He even smiled and said:

"Old Jun, aren't we going to clear things up immediately after we go bankrupt? After clearing things up, we'll distribute the money. The twenty to thirty thousand in my hands have already been lost, just like yours. Don't you believe me? Go ask Zhou Yun! He knows."

Jiaxing was still smiling, and glaring at him vigilantly. He roared like a mad lion wounded by a bullet:

"What nonsense are you talking about? There's still more than fifty thousand in your hands. As for me, I lost it for the company. It's not fair for you to do this. You cunning..."

Jiaxing was stunned by A Jun's roar. His head was full of accounts. He lowered his head, and couldn't help but become angry and listen:

"That's impossible. In short, you should first take back your losses before you speak."

In this way, the two men separated like silent, angrily trembling lions.

A few days later, the company closed its doors following rumors of a fight between A Jun and Jiaxing in the city. The entire city was stirred up by huge waves, and many related stores also went bankrupt.

However, during this period, one dark night, when Jiaxing was returning home from a smoking den, his life was ended by a few dark shadows flashing by.

Lanterns

— Leon

Over the past four or five years, my state of mind has clearly changed with the times. My interests and passions are always firmly suppressed by a heavy melancholy. What others might consider worthy of joy, I only feel with indifference. So, my friends all accuse me of being too pessimistic, and further determine that living like this will never allow me to find the true meaning of life. I admit that this determination is correct, and I have repeatedly had the urge—I want to revel, to enjoy as much as possible the things I once loved, even to rekindle the innocence of my childhood—but every attempt has always failed.

Currently, it is again the festive season for playing with lanterns. If I were still in my childhood, I don't know how much of a commotion I would cause? Recalling these things, they are still vividly alive as if they were happening right now. When I was nine or ten years old, every time this New Year's lantern festival came around, I would never let go of my dad. As soon as I put down my rice bowl, I would wipe my mouth and drag Dad to the City God Temple to buy lanterns. At that time, Dad's hair hadn't turned white yet, and his hands and feet were nimble. I held onto the hem of his sky-blue iron-woven silk gown, skipping and jumping as I walked with Dad along the cobblestone streets of the city. After walking a while, I would always steal a glance at Dad's face. He always had that smile on his face. The spring sunshine shone on his face, making his countenance and heart seem even more joyful. He would sometimes reach out and stroke my face. His hands were warm, so warm.

From the innocent little heart, a sense of gratitude would also seep out. "In the world, besides Mom, who is more kind and loving than Dad? I want to stick close to Mom and Dad all my life. I would rather not eat than let Mom and Dad leave me. Even if others buy me lanterns, I don't want them..." Wasn't that what I was thinking then? Although foolishly laughable, it came from the deepest feelings. Thinking about it now, a layer of gray and gloomy mist inevitably covers my heart, and my eyes become moist. Occasionally passing by the City God Temple, the grand scene of the lantern market, even in this year of disaster, is still no less than in those days. The styles and decorations of the lanterns are becoming more and more exquisite and beautiful due to the evolution of material civilization. However, these things can no longer have any relationship with me. Short-lived childhood slipped by like a water arrow, and who can tie it down? The living environment is sliding towards a downward direction, making it difficult to even grab some time to relax and breathe.

From now on, I can only stare at the light of the lanterns in the hands of the neighbor's children.

When I first entered the torrent of life, my Dad and Mom moved to the countryside to live. One reason was to reduce my burden of living, and the other was to return to their roots. Elderly people always have the calculations of elderly people. There are no parents in the world who don't love and care for their sons. In my childhood, I didn't want to leave Dad and Mom, and was even willing not to eat. But now, because I have to eat, I have to leave the two elderly people. Hehe, when will I be able to hold onto Dad's robe and go to the City God Temple to buy lanterns again? When will I be able to enjoy the warmth of Dad's hands again? My state of mind will never recover.

In this season of lanterns, I can only be an onlooker.

Special Article

A Visit to the Chiba Soy Sauce Industry in Japan (4)

— (Ye Xiyuan)

Noda Shoyu Co., Ltd. is famous in Japan for producing "Kikkoman" soy sauce. In addition, it also produces "Manjo" mirin. Noda's soy sauce and Nagareyama's mirin have earned extremely high praise in Japan. Its establishment was a merger of eight soy sauce brewers in Noda and Nagareyama mirin, as well as Japanese soy sauce from Incheon, making it the largest in Japan. I will briefly record the numbers as follows:

Capital: 30,000,000 yen

Total site area: 169,899 tsubo

Total building area: 70,824 tsubo

Employees: 400

Workers: 3,000

Annual production: 500,000 koku

Factories: 23

Its factory locations are naturally mostly in Noda, Chiba; in addition, they are scattered in Umenosato Village, Gyotoku Town, and Nagareyama Town in Chiba. There is also its Kansai factory in Arai Village, Kako County, Hyogo Prefecture in Kansai, a Korean factory in Songlim-ri, Incheon Prefecture, Korea, and its Fengtian factory in Ujicho, Fengtian, Manchuria. The scale can be imagined. For the benefit of its employees, Noda Shoyu Co., Ltd. also proposed 600,000 yen to establish a "Yofukai" as a hall for its employees.

Xu Wenbi's Opening

Shi Yin (1340) 10:00 AM to 11:00 AM

Opening "Yang Guifei's Regret"

Lonely Western Palace, painting resentment forever. After bathing in the hot springs, adding more fragrance. The imperial concubine sits alone on the agarwood couch, listening to the murmuring poetry of the Snow Robe Lady. Thinking that after she entered the palace and received favor, the emperor was overjoyed. Thinking that in the beginning, they swore a secret oath under the moon, the inlaid box and golden hairpin would never be forgotten. Wishing to be born together and die in the same tomb, her face like a flower, her clothes like clouds. Still remembering the sweet words in the Hall of Eternal Life, the Qingping Tune was composed in the palace. During that time, the beauties of the six palaces were colorless, leaving the favored Concubine Mei on the sidelines. Hating her eunuch Gao Lishi, who said that the emperor was not feeling well tonight. Therefore, lingering in the library, not allowing others to enter, quietly asking the concubine not to be alarmed. Yang Guifei was suspicious. The light knock of the copper ring revealed the spring light. Only knowing that the imperial bed was in a solemn palace, not knowing that Concubine Mei was serving the king. Who knew that the drums of Yuyang were connected to the sky, and the rebellion of Lushan disturbed Fanyang. Ge Shuhan was defeated by the vanguard rebels, and Tongguan was broken in panic. Suddenly, the Rainbow Skirt Song was broken, and the emperor fled to Western Shu through wind and frost. Thinking that things were rushed and helpless, Chen Yuanli was ordered to lead the six armies. Traveling to the foot of Mawei Mountain, the six armies were too rampant to move forward. Saying, alas, the dust-covered emperor has no master, and the jade is lost, and the fragrance disappears, and the heart is doubled in pain. Later, the sound of bells was heard in Jiange, breaking the intestines, and a song was even more bleak and cold in the rain. This hatred will last forever.

The beauty is re-walking, speaking her love. That day, hearing that you were sick, little sister was worried and could not relax. I, intended to serve you in person, only because your mother's family law is fierce. I'll have to wait until tonight when my mother goes to sleep, and I'll come to ask my brother. I want to ask you, why did you get this disease? Could it be because you used too much energy in the realm of lust? Talent listens. Laughs in the spring breeze. Cousin's words are not true, I am sick, but not seriously. Only because I took a walk in the cool air last night. I will surely recover in a few days, so I will not ask the doctor. Little sister listens. Her heart is relaxed. The sad guest instantly changes to joyful. Brother, I have the kindness to ask the doctor, to report that you will be relaxed as soon as you get sick. To treat you to a beautiful date and a rain and cloud.

Radio Drama Script "Temptation"

Preface

This drama was conceived by Tiehan Jun and written by Liu Yawei Jun. With the author's consent, it will be published daily. After the entire drama is published, it will be broadcast by the actors' broadcasting association. (The radio station has not been determined)

Scene 1: Driven out of the rural village by a flood mixed with hunger and cold. Time and place: a corner of a farm worker's area during a flood in a certain province in a certain year.

(Everyone sings the hoe song for about three minutes)

Old Zhang: (Calling from afar) Time to eat!

Little Lu: Big brother is calling us to eat, let's go, quickly pick up the hoes.

A Qiao: We're working so happily and now he's calling us to eat.

Little Lu: What? A Qiao, aren't you hungry?

A Qiao: Unless your stomach, Little Lu, is special, so you don't need to eat anything, my stomach can't do that!

Little Lu: A Qiao, you're always like a child, always talking upside down. When people call you to eat, you're not happy to go. When I ask you if you're hungry, you say you have to eat! What does that mean?

A Qiao: (Coyly laughs) Okay, you see, you told me to pick up the hoe, but why aren't you picking it up?

Little Lu: Forget it, let me carry both of them! (While jumping and crying) She's always so naughty~

Old Five (Shandong accent): Little Lu, you're always so happy, whenever I see you, I think of myself.

A Qiao (coyly laughing) Double Boy! (Runs away jumping)

Little Lu: Old Five, see you later.

Old Five: Don't go, don't go, let me say a few words to you, have you collected the rent for the fields?

Little Lu: They came to collect it, but these years, farming has been losing money, where do we get the money to give?

Film

Colman's New Film "The Man Who Broke the Bank at Monte Carlo" Will Be Released

Since the film "Er Nü Ying Xiong" (Children of Heroes), the love saint Colman has not had a new film released for a long time. Recently, I heard that his new work "The Man Who Broke the Bank at Monte Carlo" will be released at the Cathay Theater soon. The film is the latest production of 20th Century Fox, starring Joan Bennett. The film tells the story of a romance that occurred in Monte Carlo with a Russian royal family member. The plot is full of twists and turns, and the performance is both serious and humorous. Especially when depicting love, Colman has an amazing performance.
